Third Day of the Capital Construction Conference 68

▲ Second General Assembly Held in the Morning

The Capital Construction Committee held its second general assembly at 9:00 AM on the 17th. Attendees included Xu Chaotong, Chen Duan, Xu Zhaojun, Zhuo Yue, Mei Kechao, Yang Xixu, Lin Yunhai (represented by Lu Yougang), Zhang Renjie, Shen Zuwei, He Jian (represented by Yuan Hui), Chen Mingshu (represented by Yang Zongjiong), Lu Dipin (represented by Lu Lushan), Zhang Jianming, Lai Lian, Chen Yu, Liu Jiwen, Zhang Nanxian, Zhang Xueliang (represented by Qin Hua), Liu Wendao (represented by Dong Xiujia), He Chengjun (represented by Tang Zhi), Long Yun (represented by Wang Shu), Liu Youchen, Jiang Menglin, Gao Bingfang, Zhang Yichou, Chen Zhongsheng, Zhang Qun (represented by Shen Yi), Qin Yu, Ge Jingsi (represented by Wu Bizhi), Deng Gang, Jin Guobao, Xu Xinwu, Wei Daoming, Kong Xiangxi, Zhang Zhijiang (represented by Wang Weifan), Hong Lanyou, Liu Baichou, Shubaide, Chen Shaokuan, Xu Shiying, Wang Zhengting, etc., chaired by Zhang Renjie. After reading the will, Secretary-General Liu Jiwen reported that the number of committee members present met the legal quorum and that the meeting should begin immediately. Subsequently, Xu Xinwu, a member of the First Group Review Committee, reported on the review results of each case, and discussions began. The situation is recorded below.

Xu Xinwu, member of the First Group Review Committee, reported: (First Report) The fourteenth case reviewed by this group, proposed by Sun Ke, concerns the establishment of a commercial port in the capital; the twenty-third case proposes opening up Pukou as a commercial port; the twenty-sixth case proposes the enactment of regulations for zoning in the capital; the thirty-fifth case proposes the demarcation of the Jingpu ferry terminal area; the fifty-fifth case, proposed by Liu Jiwen, proposes drafting regulations for zoning in the capital; and the fifty-fourth case proposes a zoning plan for the capital. After review, it was decided to combine the above cases for discussion. The zoning plan proposed by Liu was approved, the zoning regulations were submitted to the Standing Committee for review, and the remainder was submitted to the Engineering Group for reference. Request for discussion. After detailed discussion by the committee members, it was resolved that the zoning plan and the principles of the regulations were approved in principle, and together with the relevant cases, they were submitted to the Standing Committee for approval. At this point, Secretary Hong Lanyou reported that there was a temporary proposal. The Chairman requested a change in the agenda, and with no objections from the members, Secretary Hong reported that the temporary proposal was submitted by Wei Daoming, Kong Xiangxi, and Jiang Menglin, requesting that Wu Jingheng, Li Shizeng, and Liu Jiwen be additionally appointed as members of the committee. The members approved the proposal. The Chairman then announced the continuation of the discussion on the First Group Review Report, which was still reported by Xu Xinwu. (Second Report) The first case, proposed by Xu Shiying, concerns expediting the construction of a water supply system; the fourth case, proposed by Liu Ruiheng, concerns the capital's water and sewage system; and the seventeenth case, proposed by Sun Ke, proposes adopting a separate sewage system. After review, it was determined that the water supply project was already being prepared by the Nanjing Municipal Government, and due to economic considerations, it was proposed to adopt a separate sewage system in principle, with the Engineering Group appointing a specialist to coordinate the design. Request for discussion. The committee members considered the review opinions to be very good and unanimously resolved to approve the review report. Xu Xinwu also reported: (Third Report) The sixth case, proposed by Wang Boqun, concerns formulating the design and restrictions for buildings along the capital's main roads to emphasize aesthetics; the ninth case, proposed by Sun Ke, proposes formulating a capital road system; the thirty-first case, proposed by Liu Jiwen, proposes defining the names of the capital's main roads; and the forty-second case, proposed by Kong Xiangxi, concerns implementing the marking of routes for each main road and public buildings. Review opinions: the principle of defining the names of the capital's main roads in Liu's case was approved, the road names were submitted to the Standing Committee for approval, and the remainder was handled by the Beijing Municipal Government. It was resolved to approve the review report. Xu Xinwu also reported: (Fourth Report) The twenty-first case, proposed by Sun Ke, concerns the increasing population of the capital, proposing to select land to build more public housing to benefit residents; and the sixty-first case, proposed by Lu Dipin, recommends borrowing funds to plan the construction of permanent and temporary housing for citizens. Review opinions: it is proposed to submit it to the Standing Committee for consideration. It was resolved to approve the review report. Xu also reported: (Fifth Report) The eighth case, proposed by Zhang Renjie, concerns dredging the Qinhuai River; and the twelfth case, proposed by Sun Ke, proposes a plan to dredge the Qinhuai River and the city moat. Review opinions: the dredging project should be handled by the Beijing Municipal Government in advance. It was resolved to approve the review report. He also reported: (Sixth Report) The thirteenth case, proposed by Sun Ke, proposes establishing parks and constructing tree-lined avenues; Kong Xiangxi also proposed promoting suburban construction and adopting a garden city plan; the fifty-third case, proposed by Liu Jiwen, proposes drafting a plan for the capital's secondary roads and tree-lined roads; and Yi Peiji also proposed adding a park specialty to the capital's municipal system. The four cases were combined for discussion. Review opinions: 1. Parks and tree-lined roads should be handled with reference to the zoning plan. All public-use addresses should be demarcated first to facilitate pricing and purchase. 2. The planning of secondary roads should be submitted to the Standing Committee for approval. It was resolved that the planning of secondary roads should be submitted to the Standing Committee for approval, and the remainder was approved according to the review opinions. Xu also reported: (Seventh Report) The nineteenth case, proposed by Sun Ke, proposed

Page 8

improving the capital's electrical wiring system. Review opinions: It should be buried at the same time as new roads and underground water pipes. It was resolved to approve the review opinions. He also reported: (Eighth Report) The twentieth case, proposed by Sun Ke, proposes improving the capital's street lighting system. Review opinions: It should be jointly reviewed and handled by the Standing Committee and the Construction Committee. It was resolved to approve the review report. He also reported (Ninth Report) The sixty-fourth case, proposed by Zhang Renjie, concerns allocating funds to complete the street lighting installation within a limited time. Review opinions: It is proposed to request the National Government to allocate funds to the Construction Committee for implementation. It was resolved to approve the review. He also reported (Tenth Report) The eighteenth case, proposed by Sun Ke, proposes using public buses as the capital's transportation vehicle equipment; the fifty-eighth case, proposed by Kong Xiangxi, concerns preparing for a municipal tram system in the capital; and the sixty-second case, proposed by Lu Dipin, concerns building a tram system in the capital to facilitate transportation. The three cases were combined for discussion. Review opinions: It should be studied by the Standing Committee. It was resolved to approve the review opinions. He also reported: (Eleventh Report) The second case, proposed by Zhang Zhijiang, concerns the construction of a public assembly hall in the capital. Review opinions: It should be reviewed by the Engineering Group and then submitted to the Standing Committee for approval. It was resolved to approve the review report. He also reported: (Twelfth Report) The tenth case, proposed by Sun Ke, proposes constructing asphalt macadam road surfaces for the capital's roads. Review opinions: It should be submitted to the Engineering Group for reference. It was resolved to approve the review opinions. (Thirteenth Report) The eleventh case, proposed by Sun Ke, proposes opening suburban roads in the capital to facilitate transportation. Review opinions: It should be designed by the Engineering Group. It was resolved to approve the review opinions (Fourteenth Report) The fifteenth case, proposed by Sun Ke, concerns specifying the location of the airport station. Review opinions: It should be jointly reviewed by the Standing Committee, the Ministry of Military Affairs, and the Ministry of Transportation to determine the address and reserve it for future use. It was resolved to approve the review opinions. (Fifteenth Report) The twenty-fifth case, proposed by Sun Ke, proposes requesting the National Government to enact urban design and zoning authorization laws. Review opinions: It is proposed to invite representatives from various provincial and municipal governments to the Standing Committee to jointly draft urban design and zoning authorization laws and submit them to the Legislative Yuan for review. It was resolved to approve the review opinions. (Sixteenth Report) The sixty-ninth case, proposed by Liu Wendao, concerns how to zone the capital's construction. Review opinions: It should be handled jointly with Liu Jiwen's proposal to draft a zoning plan for the capital. It was resolved to approve the review opinions.

Next, Yang Xixu, a member of the Third Group Review Committee, reported: (First Report) The twenty-fourth case, proposed by Sun Ke, concerns renovating the capital's silk weaving industry; the forty-first case, proposed by Kong Xiangxi, proposes promoting appropriate handicrafts in the capital; the fortieth case, proposed by Kong Xiangxi, proposes promoting industry in the capital; and the fiftieth case, proposed by Kong Xiangxi, proposes developing new industries in the capital. The four cases were combined for discussion. Review opinions: The main points of the above four cases are all to develop industry in the capital, and they are of the same nature and should be combined into one case. The fiftieth case should be the main case. The first item of measures, "Methods to be adopted for developing industry in the capital," is considered appropriate and can be adopted. The second item of measures are all practical enterprises, but they are not exclusively within the scope of capital construction and should be submitted to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce and the Beijing Municipal Government's Social Affairs Bureau for guidance. It was resolved to delete the phrase "Industries operated by foreigners are not included in this example" at the end of the first item, and the remainder was approved according to the review opinions. (Second Report) The forty-seventh case, proposed by Kong Xiangxi, concerns the capital's forest park construction plan; the forty-eighth case, proposed by Kong Xiangxi, proposes raising funds to selectively purchase land to promote construction; and the sixtieth case, proposed by Lu Dipin, proposes requesting the allocation of large sums of money to purchase private land in the capital to reorganize the land and develop municipal administration. The three cases were combined for discussion. Review opinions: The forty-eighth case should be the main case, and the established principles are all necessary and should be approved. As for the amount of land to be purchased and the funds to be allocated from the construction bonds, they cannot be decided by this committee in a short time and should be submitted to the Standing Committee for discussion. It was resolved to approve the review opinions. (Third Report) The thirty-eighth case, proposed by Kong Xiangxi, concerns establishing a rice market in the capital to revitalize commerce and regulate the people's food supply. After review, it was determined that it concerns commerce and the people's food supply and is under the purview of other specialized agencies and is not the responsibility of this committee. It should be submitted to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's Food Committee and the Beijing Municipal Government for joint handling. It was resolved to approve the review opinions. (Fourth Report) The thirty-second case, proposed by Liu Jiwen, proposes organizing a capital exposition to revitalize the capital's local area. After review, it was determined that the effect of the exposition can indeed revitalize the capital's local area, and the principles of the original case were approved. The date of the exposition will be determined separately by the Standing Committee. It was resolved to approve the review opinions. (Fifth Report) The forty-ninth case, proposed by Kong Xiangxi, proposes establishing large-scale civilian factories in the capital to relieve unemployment. After review, it was submitted to the Municipal Government for consideration and handling. It was resolved to approve the review opinions (Sixth Report) The thirty-ninth case, proposed by Kong Xiangxi, concerns opening roads in the capital and collecting fees separately from the land on both sides of the road. After review, it was determined that it is related to the Land Law and should be discussed after the Land Law is enacted. It was resolved to retain it. (Seventh Report) The forty-third case, proposed by Kong Xiangxi, concerns establishing a national goods cooperative market in the capital to promote cooperative enterprises and develop national goods. Review opinions: Since the Ministry of Industry and Commerce has already considered this case, it should be submitted to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for handling. It was resolved to approve the review opinions. (Eighth Report) The forty-seventh case, proposed by Kong Xiangxi, concerns the capital's forest park construction plan; and the fifty-ninth case, proposed by Lu Dipin, concerns developing forests in the capital. After review, it was determined that it can be approved in principle, and the detailed plan should be submitted to the Standing Committee for discussion. It was resolved to approve the review opinions.

Finally, Wei Daoming, a member of the Temporary Proposal Group Review Committee, reported: (First Report) The case proposed by Yang Xixu concerns building more affordable housing to benefit residents. Review opinions: This case has the same principles as the twenty-first case proposed by Sun Ke, which concerns the increasing population of the capital and proposes to select land to build more public housing to benefit residents, and can be combined for discussion. It was resolved to approve the review opinions. (Second Report) The capital's construction costs are enormous, and how should they be raised? Review opinions: The methods proposed in the original case are still concrete and can be submitted to the Standing Committee for adoption with other cases regarding raising funds. It was resolved to approve the review opinions. (Third Report) The sixty-eighth case concerns building the capital with the principles of simplicity, solemnity, and garden city. Review opinions: The original case is only a type of opinion on engineering forms and can be submitted to the Engineering Group for reference. It was resolved to approve the review opinions. (Fourth Report) The sixty-seventh case concerns the price of private land requisitioned for Zhongshan Road and should be returned as soon as possible. Review opinions: This case seems to be a matter of fact in municipal administration and has little to do with capital construction. It should be submitted to the Municipal Government. It was resolved to submit it to the Standing Committee for a decision on the repayment method. (Fifth Report) The case proposed by Yang Xixu concerns establishing civilian factories to relieve unemployed civilians. Review opinions: This case has the same principles as the forty-ninth case, which concerns establishing large-scale civilian factories in the capital to relieve unemployment, and can be combined for discussion. It was resolved to approve the review opinions. (Sixth Report) The sixty-sixth case concerns completing the capital plan in the shortest possible time. Review opinions: The main points of this case can be combined for discussion with the twenty-ninth case. It was resolved to approve the review opinions.) (Seventh Report) The twenty-second case proposes adding more primary and secondary schools. Review opinions: This case concerns municipal education and is proposed to be submitted to the Municipal Government for reference. It was resolved to approve the review opinions. (Eighth Report) The fifth case concerns the establishment of medical and healthcare institutions in the capital. Review opinions: This case concerns municipal sanitation and is extremely urgent. The proposed methods are also very detailed. It should be approved in principle and submitted to the Municipal Government for handling. It was resolved to approve the review opinions. (Ninth Report) The third case concerns promoting public cemeteries, banning private cemeteries, and banning the storage of coffins. Review opinions: The original case is an essential issue in municipal administration. The location of the public cemetery has already been surveyed by the Municipal Government. The case is approved in principle and submitted to the Municipal Government for handling. It was resolved to approve the review opinions. (Tenth Report) The proposal by Wang Zhengting, Wei Daoming, and Kong Xiangxi concerns allocating and borrowing a considerable portion of the Boxer Indemnity returned by various countries to fund the issuance of capital construction bonds. It was resolved to submit it to the Standing Committee for handling.

▲ Closing Ceremony Held in the Afternoon

The conference discussed each case individually, and by 1:00 PM, all cases had been completed. The closing ceremony was then held on the spot, chaired by Zhang Renjie. After the ceremony, Kong Xiangxi delivered a closing speech on behalf of the attendees, briefly stating the importance and significance of this conference. All committee members and representatives are very clear about what we should pay attention to, that is, the current capital construction must conform to the trend of the times, conform to revolutionary construction, and conform to economic principles. To be a model for national construction, so that people at home and abroad are satisfied, and the current capital construction is in accordance with the Premier's construction will, reflecting the spirit of innovation of the Chinese nation. The responsibilities and missions everyone bears are also very important. I hope that all representatives will present the central government's fighting spirit to the authorities of various provinces and cities, so that they know the central government's difficulties. The capital is the capital of the whole country and has a direct relationship with all provinces and cities. We must work together to help it complete as soon as possible. The expenses that should be shared must be remitted on time, and whether all provinces and cities can help the central government do things can also be proved by this. Whether the central government's policies are supported or not, and whether the central government has the ability to unify, will also be seen here. I would like to offer my opinions and hope that everyone will not fail this mission, and so on. Then the music was played, the ceremony was completed, and the meeting was adjourned.

Preliminary Points on the Kinship and Inheritance Sections of the Civil Code (Continued) 69

▲Hu Hanmin and Lin Sen Request a Decision from the Central Political Council

(2) What should be the age of marriage? According to the laws of various countries, in order to prevent early marriage, regulations on the age of marriage are often set. However, the standards are not consistent. Some notable examples include: Sweden, male 21, female 18; Germany, male 21, female 16; Switzerland and Norway, male 20, female 18; Prussia, male 19, female 17; France, Italy, Belgium, Romania, Netherlands, Portugal, and Hungary, male 18, female 15; Prussia, male 18, female 14; Austria, male 14, female 14; England and Spain, male 14, female 12. According to our country's general code, in ancient times, men married at 50 and women at 30; in medieval times, men took a wife at 30 and women at 20. However, the old laws did not have explicit regulations on the age of marriage. When drafting the kinship law this time, what age should be set as the age of marriage? This is the fourth point to be decided in advance. (3) What should be the restrictions on marriage between relatives? According to the laws of various countries, the restrictions on marriage between relatives vary. Some define the scope as direct blood relatives, direct relatives by marriage, and collateral blood relatives within the third degree, such as the Japanese Civil Code. Others define the scope as direct blood relatives, siblings, half-siblings, and direct relatives by marriage, such as the German Civil Code. Still others define the scope as direct blood relatives, siblings, and half-siblings, such as the Soviet Russian Civil Code. Some only define the scope as direct blood relatives and siblings, such as the Siamese Civil Code draft. The old laws of our country had very strict restrictions on marriage between relatives: 1. The wives and concubines of relatives of the same clan, whether divorced or remarried, were prohibited from marrying. 2. Half-siblings, even if they were not from the same clan, were also prohibited from marrying. 3. Marriages between relatives of different generations were prohibited. 4. Even if they were not relatives, marriages between those with obvious generational differences were also prohibited. How should our kinship law be regulated? This is the fifth point to be decided in advance. (4) How should the marital property system be regulated? According to the legislative examples of various countries, the marital property system can be divided into three types: 1. Community property system: The husband and wife each contribute a part or all of their property to form community property, with the husband having the right to manage it, but its disposal requires the wife's consent. 2. Joint management system: The husband and wife combine their property, with the husband having the right to manage it, but each retains ownership. 3. Separate property system: The ownership and management rights of the husband and wife's property are independent, and the family expenses are borne jointly by the husband and wife. Furthermore, the laws of various countries either designate one of the above systems as the statutory property system, which is deemed to be adopted if the parties have no other agreement, or set up several other systems outside the statutory system as standards for concluding property contracts, from which the parties can choose one, or do not set up the above standards and allow the parties to freely agree on their property relationship by contract. How should our kinship law be regulated? This is the sixth point to be decided by public vote. (5) Can the issue of concubines be resolved by separate legislation? According to our country's system of concubinage, what is the status of the concubines who have been taken and their children? If there are no explicit provisions, it is difficult to apply. Can this be resolved by separate legislation? This is the seventh point to be decided by public vote. (6) If the family system needs to be defined, how should it be regulated? The kinship laws of various countries adopt either the family system or the individual system. Those who adopt the family system regard the family as the basis of society, and the law recognizes the existence of the family system. Those who adopt the individual system regard the individual as the basis of society, and the law does not recognize the existence of the family system. However, in countries that adopt the family system, some combine the clan with the family, such as Japan. Anyone who inherits the family also inherits the clan. Although there is a so-called family in our country in practice, there are no clear regulations on the organization and status of the family in law. Furthermore, the clan is the clan, and the family is the family. The clan refers to the relationship in the system, while the family refers to the actual organization. Should the family system be regulated in this drafting of the kinship law? This is the eighth point to be decided in advance. If the family system is regulated, the laws of various countries either take the authority of the head of the family as the basis, such as the Japanese Civil Code, or take the common life as the basis, such as the Swiss Civil Code. The former's so-called family takes those under the jurisdiction of the head of the family as members and those within the scope of the head of the family's authority as the scope. The latter's so-called family is based on people living together and is established out of the need for support and guardianship, not focusing on the rights of the head of the family, but focusing on the obligations of the head of the family. If our kinship law needs to regulate the family system, how should it be regulated? This is the ninth point to be decided in advance.

▲Points to be Decided in Advance on Inheritance Law (1) Should the inheritance of the ancestral temple be regulated? Is the inheritance of the estate predicated on the inheritance of the ancestral temple? According to our country's clan, the male line has always been emphasized. After three generations, the eldest son of the princes inherited the title of prince, and the descendants of the collateral lines were of various kinds. The Zhou people used the method of the great clan and the small clan to consolidate their group. Later Confucian scholars spoke of rites and mostly focused on the clan law. The emperors of past dynasties also compromised in this regard. Therefore, the clan law became the clan law, not only practiced by the collateral descendants of princes and nobles, but also imitated by ordinary people. Through inheritance and changes, it has become the clan system of today. Should the inheritance of the ancestral temple be regulated in this drafting of the inheritance law in our country? This is the first point to be decided in advance. If the inheritance of the ancestral temple should be regulated, it should also be clearly stipulated whether the person who inherits the ancestral temple is the person who inherits the estate, so as to avoid doubts. This is the second point to be decided in advance. (2) How should the scope and order of heirs and their shares be regulated? The laws of various countries are very inconsistent regarding the scope and order of heirs and their shares. Taking the German and Japanese civil codes as examples, Germany divides heirs into two types: designated heirs and statutory heirs. Statutory heirs are limited to spouses and direct relatives. The order of inheritance, except for the spouse of the deceased, varies depending on whether there are relatives of the first or second degree. The direct descendants of the deceased are the first in order, the parents of the deceased and their direct descendants are the second in order, the grandparents of the deceased and their direct descendants are the third in order, and the great-grandparents of the deceased and their direct descendants are the fourth in order. The fifth order and below are the distant ancestors of the deceased and their direct descendants. The share of the heir, except for the surviving spouse of the deceased, varies depending on whether there are relatives of the first or second degree. The rest are divided equally according to the order of precedence, with the closest relatives receiving the most. Japan also limits the scope to spouses and direct relatives, but the direct descendants of the deceased are the first in order, the spouse of the deceased is the second in order, the direct ascendants of the deceased are the third in order, and the head of the household is the fourth in order. The principle of their share is the same as in Germany. However, when there are several direct descendants, the share of illegitimate children and children born out of wedlock is one-half of that of legitimate children. As for the old laws of our country, 1. The inheritance of the estate is limited to direct descendants. Spouses and direct ascendants have no right to inherit the estate. 2. Those direct descendants who can inherit the estate are limited to men. Women can only inherit the property of a deceased household, but have no right to inherit the estate. 3. In the analysis and distribution of the estate, except for illegitimate children who are given half according to the amount of children, both legitimate and illegitimate children, male and female, are divided equally according to the number of children. Since the circumstances at home and abroad are so different, how should our inheritance law be regulated? This is the third point to be decided in advance. (To be continued)

Zhejiang Provincial Party Department Requests Protest Against Japanese Fleet's Arrival in China 70

The Zhejiang Provincial Executive Committee believes that the large Japanese fleet's arrival in China and its holding of spring exercises near the Zhoushan Islands in Zhejiang Province is an insult to our country. In addition to telegraphing the Central Government to lodge a serious protest against Japan, it also telegraphed the Dinghai County District Executive Committee and the Zhenhai County Executive Committee to quickly report the details of the Japanese fleet's spring exercises in Zhoushan. The following are the two telegrams: (1) To the esteemed Central Executive Committee, we have learned that Japanese imperialism has long harbored ambitions to invade China. This time, taking advantage of the Central Government's suppression of Yan and Feng, it has spared no effort to resort to its old tricks, sending a large fleet of warships to China. Its intentions are self-evident. All Chinese people have long been indignant. Now, reports state that the country's warships will hold large-scale spring exercises near Zhoushan Island on the 16th of this month. After reading this, we are furious. Its contempt for our country's sovereignty and its violation of international law are extreme. If this can be tolerated, the country will not be a country. Therefore, we telegraph Your Committee to quickly transfer and instruct to lodge serious negotiations and find ways to stop it. This committee vows to lead all comrades and the people of the province as a backing to avenge this humiliation and defend national rights. The urgent situation cannot be described enough. The Zhejiang Provincial Executive Committee respectfully bows. (2) Urgent to Dinghai County Directly Subordinate District Party Department and Zhenhai County Party Department, reports state that Japanese warships will hold spring exercises near our country's Zhoushan Islands today. We hope that you will quickly and accurately investigate and report the details. Do not delay. The Provincial Executive Committee bows.

The Central Government Abolishes the Fujian Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau 71

The Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee previously learned that the Fujian Provincial Civil Affairs Department had established a Fujian Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee in Xiamen, with Dai Jinhua as the director, using registration as a pretext to extort overseas Chinese, and had been repeatedly accused. Furthermore, its name and nature contradicted the organizational regulations of the Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee. It had submitted a request to the Central Government to transfer the order to the province to abolish it. After the Central Government's 36th resolution, the Fujian Provincial Government was ordered to change the name of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee under its jurisdiction to avoid confusion with the name and functions of the Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee. As for all its handling procedures, it still had to be reported to the Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee for record. A letter was sent to the National Government to transfer and instruct compliance. Later, a letter was received from the Central Secretariat, stating that it had been approved by the National Government's Civil Affairs Office and that the National Government had issued a report from the Fujian Provincial Government, according to the Civil Affairs Department, to change the name of the Fujian Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee to the Fujian Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau, to draft a simple charter, and to prepare a separate budget. A copy of the original document was sent for reference. The Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee believed that after reviewing the bureau's charter, the scale was too large and still contradicted the committee's organizational regulations. It submitted another request to the Central Government to transfer and instruct it to change to the Fujian Overseas Chinese Compatriots Reception Center. The Central Government approved the transfer to the Executive Yuan for investigation and handling. Recently, the Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee sent personnel to investigate. The bureau had not changed its name and was still called the Xiamen Fujian Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee, and it had harassed overseas Chinese. Therefore, it submitted another request to the Central Government to explicitly abolish it. Now, a reply letter has been received from the Central Secretariat, stating that according to the Executive Yuan's report, the Fujian Provincial Government has been ordered to comply. Therefore, the Xiamen Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau will be abolished soon.

The Situation in Western Hunan Expands 72

▲Li Guojun's Troops Collude with the Guizhou Army

▲He Jian Dispatches More Troops to Suppress

Changsha correspondence, Chen Hanzhang, the brigade commander of the Independent 8th Brigade, was assassinated in Hongjiang last month and died shortly after his injuries flared up. Li Guojun, the commander of the 3rd Regiment of the brigade, was originally the mastermind behind Chen's assassination. Therefore, the day after Chen was assassinated, he led the entire unit from his garrison in Zhijiang to attack Qianyang and seize Hongjiang. Within three days, he was repelled by the 1st and 2nd Regiments led by Chen Wo, the acting brigade commander of the brigade, and Hongjiang was restored. Internal infighting led to the war between Hunan and Guizhou. The reason why Li's regiment dared to rebel this time was that they had colluded with Xie Bin of the 10th Division stationed in Tianzhu, Guizhou, and Yao Fengting and Tang Qingyun, the notorious bandits of Hunan and Guizhou. Therefore, after Li's troops were defeated and left Hongjiang, Xie Bin's troops advanced from Tianzhu and stationed in Huaihua and Zhijiang in Hunan Province to assist Li's regiment. They made an appointment with Yao and Tang's bandits to launch a fierce attack on Qianyang. Chen Wo personally led the 1st Regiment and Xiong Pinjun's 2nd Regiment, as well as the special artillery engineering battalion, to fight desperately. They attacked each other for twelve days, and both sides suffered heavy casualties, especially Chen Wo's troops. Therefore, on the 12th, they abandoned Qianyang and retreated to Hongjiang. Hongjiang is a commercial port area and has no defenses. Therefore, when Xie and Li's troops pursued and approached, Chen Wo withdrew from Hongjiang again on the 13th and concentrated in Suining to reorganize and wait for reinforcements. After receiving the report, He Jian believed that Xie's division openly aided the rebellious troops and occupied Hongjiang, which was not something that friendly troops should do. He has telegraphed Xie Bin again, ordering him to leave the border of Hunan immediately and not to interfere in the affairs of the rebellious troops. Otherwise, it is his duty to take appropriate self-defense measures. It is difficult to determine whether Xie will leave Hunan because he has not received a reply. However, in order to thoroughly resolve the rebellious troops, He has decided to transfer four regiments to assist Chen Wo in formally suppressing Li's regiment. The transferred troops are one regiment each from Dai Douyuan and Peng Weiren's brigades of the 16th Division, one regiment from Li Xuan's regiment of the 15th Division, and one regiment from the 1st Garrison Army. Chen Wo's two regiments are assigned to the middle route, Dai's brigade and Chen's regiment are assigned to the right wing, and they are to coerce the left side of Hongjiang and Qianyang from Xupu and Chenxi. Peng's brigade and Li Xuan's regiment are assigned to the left wing, and they are to attack the right side of Hong and Qian from Wugang. He has also telegraphed Mao Guangxiang, the chairman of Guizhou Province, requesting him to order Wang Jialie, the deputy commander of the army, to attack Tianzhu and pursue them from behind. In order to unify the command of the Hunan army, he will telegraph Luo Fanying, the commander of the 16th Division, to rush back to Changsha from Quanzhou on the 15th to plan the suppression. Luo Fanying will be responsible for the command in that area in the future. Luo is expected to leave for Baoqing in two or three days to arrange everything. It is feared that the armies of Hunan and Guizhou will inevitably clash as a result.

Zhu and Mao Capture Xinfeng 73

▲The County Magistrate Died in Battle

▲The Communist Bandits Slaughtered the City Terribly

Nanchang communication on the 15th, the communist bandits Zhu and Mao, on the 7th and 8th, fled back from Nanxiong and Shixing to Dayu and Xinfeng, causing terrible burning and killing. When Zhu's bandits fled from Xinfeng and Nankang to Guangdong last month, Wu Zhaofeng, the county magistrate of Xinfeng, was quite courageous and personally supervised the team to block and suppress them, so the county territory was preserved. Zhu's bandits hated him deeply, so this time they attacked Xinfeng with all their strength. Their main force was about four or five thousand people, with more than three thousand guns, and their momentum was very fierce. After hearing the alarm, County Magistrate Wu Zhaofeng still supervised Police Captain Wang Tanxun and led the police and security team of about two or three hundred people to resist the enemy. The battle was fierce, but because the number of enemies was too large, they were taken advantage of by the bandits. County Magistrate Wu and Police Captain Wang both ran out of ammunition and were isolated, and died in battle. The city of Xinfeng was captured by the bandits on the 10th. The county government, the party department, and all the public buildings were burned to the ground. Many gentry and businessmen were killed. The cruelty of their trampling was unprecedented. Yesterday, the provincial government received a telegram from those who fled from the county to Ganzhou, requesting that troops be sent quickly to suppress them. Chairman Lu and Commander-in-Chief Jin have telegraphed the Yang, Xiao, Peng, and Yu regiments in southern Jiangxi to quickly suppress them. At the same time, Xie Renzheng and others from Xinfeng who were traveling in the province also received a telegram from the Ganzhou fellow villagers association, reporting the situation of the bandits capturing the county seat and the county magistrate dying in battle. The telegram said, "Zhu and Mao's bandits, on the ash day, led four or five thousand people to capture the county seat. County Magistrate Wu Zhaofeng and Police Captain Wang Tanxun were killed, the county government was burned, and many officials, businessmen, and merchants were brutally killed. They are still entrenched and trampling wildly. In addition to telegraphing the provincial government to send troops to encircle and suppress them, please ask you to quickly petition the provincial government to save the people. The Xinfeng County Fellow Villagers Association in Ganzhou respectfully bows."

▲Transferred to Tai'an Under the Control of Ma Hongkui

Jinan correspondence, Gao Guizi's troops have been surrounded by the provincial army in Zhucheng and Juxian for nearly two months since February 20th. Tracing the National Lawyers Association's Representative Assembly 76

The Second National Lawyers Association's Representative Assembly was held in Hankou on April 1st of this year. It was prepared by the three public associations of Wuchang, Xiakou, and Shanghai, and welcomed representatives from various provinces and regions. Because the legal quorum was not met, it was rescheduled to be held on April 3rd. A total of delegates attended, Shen Xiaoxiang (Minhou), Wang Yanwu (Xinyang), Qiu Weizhen, Huang Genshi (Changsha), Liu Zuwang (Shanghai and Wuxian), Yu Zhongluo (Shanghai), Hu Zhen (Dantu), Ge Fenglai (Wuhu), Hu Jiuluan (Jiujiang), Mu Ziyi (Yichang), Chen Tingzhen, Xiao Chengsong, Chen Bangben (Huanggang), Wu Mai (Jiangning), Wang Shengwu (Anqing), Guo Zongxie, Su Daoheng, Sun Chunhai, Yang Zailin (Wuchang), Ge Xiujian (Shaoyang), Zhang Jixin, Tang Zhang, Chen Yue, Huang Naitong, Wang Zhonghai (Hangxian), Xiao Xiang (Liaoning), Li Guojiao (Qingdao), Xiao Buyun (Ganxian), Wang Fengshi (Xiangyang), Wang Zunsan (Tianjin), Guo Depei (Nanchang), Liu Liumin (Xiakou and Chengdu), Luo Zhizhu, Wang Zhaoxiang (Xiakou), a total of 23 public associations, 34 representatives attended. At 2:00 p.m. on the 2nd, a preparatory meeting was held. Representatives from various provinces and regions had arrived. Chairman Liu Liumin discussed the opening of the meeting and elected Liu Liumin, Guo Zongxie, Shen Xiaoxiang, Hu Zhen, and Liu Zuwang as the presidium. At 10:00 a.m. on the 3rd, the opening ceremony was held in the grand auditorium of the Hankou General Chamber of Commerce. All the representatives attended. Representatives from the party, government, judiciary, military, academia, and the press were sent to attend. The presidium announced the opening of the meeting and delivered speeches. After the ceremony, representatives from all walks of life gave speeches. The meeting adjourned at 2:00 p.m. Lunch and photography were enjoyed.

At 4:00 p.m. on the afternoon of the 3rd, a proposal review committee was held in the conference hall of the Xiakou Lawyers Association. It was divided into four groups. The first group reviewed legal proposals, and Yu Zhongluo was elected as the director of the review. Huang Genshi, Zhang Jixin, Mu Ziyi, Yang Zailin, Xiao Chengsong, Li Guojiao, Zhang Mo, and Liu Liumin were review committee members. The second group reviewed judicial recommendation proposals, and Hu Zhen was elected as the director of the review. Qiu Weizhen, Tang Zhang, Sun Chunhai, Chen Tingzhen, Xiao Buyun, Wang Zunsan, and Wang Zhaoxiang were review committee members. The third group reviewed lawyer association proposals, and Liu Zuwang was elected as the director of the review. Huang Naitong, Su Daoheng, Wang Zhonghai, Hu Jiuluan, Luo Zhizhu, Wu Mai, and Ge Xiujian were review committee members. The fourth group reviewed lawyer association and social or other proposals, and Shen Xiaoxiang was elected as the director of the review. Chen Yue, Wang Shengwu, Chen Bangben, Ge Fenglai, Xiao Xiang, Wang Fengshi, and Wang Yanwu were review committee members. After the directors and committee members of each group were elected, they began to review the proposals in groups. A total of 86 proposals were received. At 8:00 p.m. on the 3rd, the first meeting was held. 21 representatives attended, and Hu Zhen was elected as the chairman. The rules of procedure and 11 proposals were adopted. At 10:00 a.m. on the 4th, the second meeting was held. At 2:00 p.m., the third meeting was continued. 22 representatives attended, and Liu Zuwang was the chairman. 25 proposals were adopted, among which there was a heated debate on legal proposals and the jury and assessor system. As a result, the entire case was retained. At 10:00 a.m. on the 5th, the fourth meeting was held. At 2:00 p.m., the fifth meeting was continued. 25 representatives attended, and Shen Xiaoxiang was the chairman. 51 proposals were adopted, among which there was a detailed discussion on social cases and foreign affairs, as well as the association's organizational key cases. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 p.m., and the chairman announced the closing. On the evening of the 5th, the Wuchang and Xiakou Lawyers Associations hosted a banquet to welcome the representatives of the provincial and regional lawyers associations, and invited the chief judges of the local courts to accompany them. During the banquet, Wu Mai gave a speech on the situation of foreign propaganda, which was very touching. At 9:00 a.m. on the 6th, the first executive committee meeting of the second session was held. Committee members Guo Zongxie, Wang Shengwu, Liu Liumin, Wang Zunsan, Liu Zuwang, Hu Zhen, and Wu Mai (three of whom also served as proxies) attended. Substitute committee members Shen Xiaoxiang and Luo Zhizhu attended. On the 9th, the representatives took the Dehe and Dali ships and left Hankou that day.

Important News 2

Xiamen Cracks Down on Communist Organization 77

Xiamen Correspondence: Although communist parties have been secretly active in this city, there have been no violent riots. However, there have been instances of distributing leaflets and shouting slogans. Recently, after vigorous investigation by the Zhangzhou-Xiamen Garrison Headquarters and the Xiamen Public Security Bureau, a communist organization was successfully cracked down on at No. 9 Qinglong Temple on the 9th of this month. Initially, Yang Zhiguo, a policeman from the First Police Station of the Third Precinct, was conducting a household registration survey. When he arrived in front of No. 9 Qinglong Temple, two young men in Western suits suddenly avoided him. Yang was suspicious and entered the premises for inspection. Inside, there was a young man in his twenties, with several clothes and wooden boxes placed in the corner of the room, appearing as if they had just been moved in. Yang ordered the young man to open them for inspection, but the young man attempted to escape. Yang stopped him and then found a communist leaflet next to a wooden box. When asked where he came from, the young man hesitated for a long time and replied that he did not know. Yang ordered him to open the box for inspection. Upon opening one box, thousands of communist leaflets were found under a leather jacket, wrapped in worn-out clothing. Yang then ordered the police to arrest the young man and escort him and the boxes to the Third Precinct. After examining each item, a total of nine large boxes were found, containing over ten thousand communist-printed and mimeographed reactionary leaflets, and several hundred reactionary books. There were also three boxes of biscuits in a net basket, which, when opened, were also communist leaflets. In addition, there were two boxes of candles, with only a dozen or so candles on the top layer, and the rest filled with leaflets from the Communist Fujian Youth League. Furthermore, three important communist documents were also seized. Due to the importance of the matter, the police station immediately sealed off the house at No. 9 and sent the seized communist items along with the young man to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. According to the young man's confession, his name was Lian Jinhai, he was nineteen years old, and from Longyan. When asked about the source of the boxes and items, he claimed that he was hired by a friend to transport luggage to Xiamen, and he was unaware of the contents and illiterate. The police station is still conducting a rigorous interrogation. It is said that the young man was wearing silk clothes and appeared quite cultured, unlike someone from the working class.

Furthermore, at 7:00 AM on the 9th, many people suddenly distributed communist leaflets on Kaiyuan Road and shouted slogans. By the time the police arrived, they had already dispersed. On the night of the 8th, there were also people distributing communist leaflets near the Yanping Theater on Gulangyu. Liu Zhu, Lai Chen Ya, and Qiu Yazhi, who all appeared to be workers, were arrested by the Public Works Bureau and handed over to the Garrison Headquarters Military Law Department for interrogation on the 10th. (11th)

Guangdong Provincial Government Decides to Form Four Security Brigades 78

▲ An Office Will Be Established Under the Provincial Government

▲ The Navy Will Dispatch Additional Duan-Class Warships to Protect Waterways

Guangzhou Correspondence: Recently, due to the deployment of troops to Guangxi Province, most of the army has been sent to the front lines. Bandits in various regions have been contemplating uprisings. Recently, the Zhu Mao communist bandits in the North River took advantage of the emptiness of the garrison in Nanxiong and successively captured the counties of Shixing and Renhua. The Qinlian, Gaozhou, and Leizhou areas of the South Road have been repeatedly harassed by bandits. Most recently, Yangchun Bay in Yangjiang County was also occupied by bandits. The authorities previously planned to organize a provincial defense army specifically responsible for suppressing bandits in the region. However, due to various reasons, it was not implemented immediately. Recently, with the increasing disturbances caused by bandits in various rivers, the training of local armed forces has become urgent. Yesterday, Chen Mingshu, the chairman of the provincial government, proposed at the 68th provincial affairs meeting that the provincial government organize four security brigades, with a total of 6,000 personnel. Two brigades will be established first, stationed in the northeast and two rivers for training. Initially, 4,000 rifles and 12 machine guns will be purchased, requiring over 600,000 yuan, which will be allocated from the provincial treasury. Due to the urgency of the situation, the arms purchase proposal was submitted for a public vote first and immediately approved. According to the organizational structure of this security brigade, each brigade will consist of 1,500 personnel. The soldiers will be recruited by the county magistrates from able-bodied men within their counties, aged between eighteen and twenty-five, and in good physical condition. The method of recruiting by region stipulates that each county in the Qinlian area will recruit 40 men, each county in the Gaozhou and Leizhou-Yangjiang area will recruit 30 men, and each county in the North River and East River areas will recruit 15 men. They must be selected and sent to the province by April 31st. A security brigade training center will also be established to provide specialized training. After several months of graduation, they will be transferred to various counties to assist local police and protect the area. In the future, an office may be established under the provincial government to command them directly, reporting directly to the provincial government. As for the security of river and sea lanes, the Fourth Fleet will be responsible for dispatching additional Duan-class warships to prevent pirates from intercepting merchant ships. In Guzhen Caobu in Zhongshan County, pirates had previously appeared. Although they have been dispersed, to prevent bandits from regrouping, two warships have been dispatched to be stationed there permanently. In addition to recalling Duan-class warships to patrol the key points of the three mountains and sea entrances outside Guangzhou City, barracks will be built and marines stationed there. The waterways of the West River will be divided into four sections: the Zhujiang Warship will be responsible for security from Wuzhou to Ducheng, the Zhunjie Warship from Ducheng to Zhaoqing, the Jiangg Warship from Zhaoqing to Sanshui, the Haiqiang Warship from Sanshui to Chancun, and the warships attached to the city from Chancun to the provincial capital. In addition to designating the warships, an inspection warship will be dispatched to visit each section of the warship in turn for evaluation. (April 10th)

Eastern Railway Electricity Rights Meeting Approaching 79

▲ Mo Dehui Plans a Compromise Solution

▲ The Russian Side No Longer Insists on its Proposal

Harbin Correspondence, 9th: Mo Dehui, on behalf of the Northeast Communications Committee, proposed six points of opinion on the settlement of electricity rights in the Eastern Railway Council. The Russian side did not agree to several items, such as inspecting outbound telegrams. Therefore, on the 21st of last month, the various telegraph bureaus along the line restored their original state. The Communications Committee, fearing that the electricity rights meeting would not be convened and that the power would be completely handed over, leaving no control, retained at least two or three people in each telegraph bureau to monitor the actions of the Russian staff and secretly maintain the intention of inspecting telegrams, while still sending and receiving commercial telegrams to maintain national rights. However, the Russian side was dissatisfied with this, so several days ago, an incident occurred in the Ang'angxi telegraph office in which Chinese staff were expelled and refused entry to work. Later, with the protection of military and police, they were able to re-enter work. Recently, the Russian side believed that if the electricity rights issue was not resolved through necessary procedures at a meeting, the Northeast communications authorities would continue to refuse to release the rights quickly. Therefore, they expressed the following to the six opinions of the Communications Committee: (1) Inspecting outbound telegrams can be changed to inspecting commercial telegrams; administrative telegrams of the railway itself must not be inspected and should be passed through at any time. (2) Equal employment is not an issue; it will be handled by the Eastern Railway Electric Affairs Office and submitted to the Council for decision. (3) Commercial telegrams will not be received by the Eastern Railway and will be sent and received by the Chinese telegraph bureau. Those forwarded through the Eastern Railway will be paid a transit fee by the Chinese side, but the rates for international telegrams to Vladivostok and Moscow must not be increased to avoid affecting Russian merchants. (4) The Chinese side can set up a telegraph bureau between the Eastern Railway's Class A and B stations, provided it does not harm the railway telegraph offices. (5) The electricity fee accounts must be checked by a joint Chinese-Russian committee, and then a section of time will be determined from which year to which year for the inspection period. (6) Long-distance telephones are permitted to be redeemed by China at a price. (7) The electricity rights meeting can be convened immediately. The Communications Committee believes that although the Russian side has agreed to inspect commercial telegrams, since it has agreed to no longer receive commercial telegrams, what telegrams will China inspect in the future? As for international telegram fees, as part of China's administrative affairs, it is difficult to handle the level of not increasing fees, regardless of whether foreigners are involved. Since there are still many differences in other items, it has not yet been approved even after receiving the information. Recently, Mo Dehui, in a detached position, drafted a compromise solution, adopting the opinions of the Communications Committee and the points insisted upon by the Russian side, and drafted eight solutions, which were telegraphed to the Communications Committee yesterday to solicit their agreement. The Communications Committee has held a meeting today to review it and will reply in about two or three days. If the Communications Committee approves it, Mo will no longer seek the Russian side's opinion. If the Russian side also approves it, the Council can order the Railway Bureau to select personnel and convene an electricity rights meeting with the Communications Committee according to this method. In short, the electricity rights meeting, for the sake of overall power, Russia will have to make some concessions in order to comply.

Qingpu 80

Limiting Rice Prices and Preparing for Price Stabilization: The rice prices in this county are soaring daily, making it very difficult for the poor to make a living. The local administrative authorities of this county have convened a meeting of various agencies to discuss limiting rice prices and preparing for price stabilization. A general order has been issued to the Chamber of Commerce and rice industry representatives to order all rice merchants to sell at fair prices and not to hoard or raise prices arbitrarily. A date has been set to discuss the method of price stabilization and open branches in various districts to comfort the people.

Young Girl Enters a Nunnery to Avoid Marriage: Qian, a resident of a town in Qingpu, has a daughter named Xiaomei, who is currently twenty years old. Two years ago, her uncle acted as matchmaker and betrothed her to Shen from the same town. Shen chose a date for the wedding on the 24th of next month. However, the girl learned that Shen had lost his job this year, was unemployed, and addicted to smoking and gambling, so she was very dissatisfied. She asked her father to cancel the engagement, but her father refused and scolded her, saying, "As long as I am alive, the marriage cannot be changed." Upon hearing this, the girl was extremely frustrated. Suddenly, on the morning of the fifteenth day, she took her jewelry and ran away from home, leaving a letter stating, "I urge my father not to worry and search for me. I have decided not to marry again and am going to choose a nunnery in the Hangzhou-Huzhou area to become a nun." Since discovering that his daughter had run away, Shen immediately sent people to inquire at various nunneries in the Hangzhou-Huzhou area and went to Shanghai to place an advertisement to find her. It is unknown whether she will be found.
