Complete Plan (6) 105

7 Moral Education

First, the standards for moral education should be stipulated by the Ministry of Education based on the educational purpose and the educational development of children's native place determined by the political program, by grade in elementary schools and kindergartens.

Second, the objectives of moral education stipulated by the Ministry of Education should focus on unity. The first step should be to hire experts to first set the objectives, and then analyze the objectives into several detailed items that conform to each action of a person or become each habit. The second step is to rank them in order of difficulty of development and estimate the value of each item to be developed in each grade. The third step is to ask experienced and excellent teachers across the country to evaluate their value (either by grade or by quantity). The fourth step is to statistically analyze the results of the third step and rearrange the additions and subtractions. The fifth step is to compile usage methods and add examples of several implementation methods and performance evaluation methods, etc. The sixth step is to print and publish it and order it as the national elementary education moral education standard.

Third, the Education Department of each province should investigate special needs in the social customs of the province, increase supplementary items and implementation methods based on the moral education standards set by the Ministry of Education, and submit them to the Ministry of Education for implementation. The procedure for ordering should refer to the previous article.

Fourth, each city and county should formulate moral education matters and implementation methods for each year, month, and week based on national and provincial standards, and with reference to the special needs of the local area, and submit them to the Education Department for implementation. The procedure for ordering should refer to the previous article.

Fifth, the detailed items, matters, and implementation methods stipulated in the preceding three articles should include the entire life of students. All aspects of training students' autonomy, actively developing good habits, correcting special bad habits, using extracurricular activities, contacting families, guiding students to assist family work, and developing discipline in daily life, and the standards and methods for assessing character should be taken into account. In particular, elementary school students should be immersed in the cultivation of the Three Principles of the People from an early age.

Sixth, the methods for guiding practice and assessing performance must be precisely stipulated in order to implement them effectively.

Seventh, elementary schools that fail to organize party scouts do not need to wear uniforms. If the student's family can afford to have the elementary school students wear uniforms, foreign raw materials must not be used. Party scout clothing and supplies should be limited to domestic goods, except for unavoidable foreign goods such as camera lenses.

Eighth, the style of elementary school uniforms can be determined by the Education Department of each province based on local conditions, and cheap and easy-to-make styles can be submitted to the Ministry of Education for implementation.

8 Expenses 106

First, elementary schools and kindergartens should not charge tuition fees as a principle. In places where life is prosperous, fees may be charged at the discretion of the school. The amount of fees should be from one jiao to one yuan per semester, and each city and county should formulate separate regulations for each elementary school and kindergarten based on the local living conditions, and submit them to the higher-level education administrative organs for approval and implementation.

Second, in elementary schools and kindergartens that charge fees, free places should still be provided for poor students.

Third, elementary schools and kindergartens that charge fees should not have discriminatory treatment for fee-paying students and free students, and should not use fee-paying and free as a basis for class division.

Fourth, the tuition revenue of elementary schools and kindergartens in each province, city, and county shall not be listed as recurring expenses, but should be used for special accounting and deposited, and used exclusively for the improvement and expansion of elementary schools in each city and county that are not well-equipped, or for special subsidies to poor students.

Fifth, elementary schools and kindergartens must not collect miscellaneous fees from students. If the elementary school and kindergarten acts as an agent for students in consuming goods such as paper, pens, notebooks, work materials, and experimental drugs, it may stipulate a compromise number and submit it to the competent education administrative organ to collect from students. If there is a surplus, it shall be submitted to the competent education administrative organ and used separately for the improvement and expansion of the equipment of each elementary school and kindergarten.

Sixth, except for special circumstances and prior submission to the competent education administrative authorities for temporary fundraising from student families for books, construction, etc., students must not be charged long-term reading fees, sports fees, construction fees, etc.

Seventh, party scouts' personal items are provided by the students themselves.

Nine Courses 107

First, when the trial period of the provisional curriculum standards expires, the Ministry of Education should, based on the results of the trial, revise and compile them into formal curriculum standards. At the same time, based on these standards, it should formulate editing standards for textbooks, teaching books, reference books, and self-study books. It should also compile and print model textbooks, prepare wall charts, and manufacture suitable teaching aids to serve as models for merchants to imitate.

Second, each provincial education department should, based on the curriculum standards, investigate the local conditions of each place in its province, formulate curricula. When formulating, a committee may be organized to handle it. The organizational outline of the committee shall be promulgated by the Ministry of Education.

Third, the content of the primary school curriculum should be formulated in detail according to the provisions of the primary school curriculum standards. However, it may not be divided into subjects, but take designed activities as the warp and the teaching materials of each subject as the weft, arranged in sequence, in order to apply. The content items can be divided into "objectives," "activities," and "achievement limits," and can be supplemented with "time allocation," "teaching examples," etc. The main points are as follows:

1. Objectives: Define the various things that should be strived for in each grade or stage in a specific and itemized manner as objectives, to serve as a guide for teachers to guide children's learning. The compilation method can be to first mix the original subject objectives of the primary school curriculum standards, and then specifically analyze them and list them as several items, separately compiled as the objectives of a certain year or each stage.

2. Activities: Similar to the objectives, specify the various activities of each grade or stage item by item. The compilation method can be based on the original "task requirements for each academic year" of each subject in the primary school curriculum standards, linking, mixing, and analyzing them into several designed activities containing specific teaching materials, separately compiled as the activity items of a certain year or stage. The most important thing to pay attention to in this item is that all abstract standards mentioned in the curriculum standards, such as "local...", "daily...", "main...", etc., should be specifically defined as specific teaching materials.

3. Achievement Limits: Also specify separately by grade or stage. The compilation method should be in accordance with the original standard of "minimum limit," taking into account local conditions, and defining it as the achievement limit for a certain year or stage.

4. Time Allocation: The determined number of hours and time arrangement methods adopted in this district can be specified for schools to follow.

5. Teaching Examples: Specify various teaching examples separately by grade or stage for teachers to refer to. Detailed records of reference books, teaching aids, and their usage, experimental methods, and test examination methods should also be included.

A Glimpse of Suggestions 108

▲Advocating the Abolition of Graduation School Exams and Replacing Them with Unified Examinations 109

Wu Yourong, Representative of Overseas Chinese from Taiwan

Respectfully submitted to all Provincial Education Directors, Municipal and County Education Bureau Directors, and National Education Experts by the Shanghai Shen Bao: Yesterday, I submitted a petition to Chairman Jiang Wenri of the National Education Conference, stating the disadvantages of graduation school exams and the reasons for replacing them with unified examinations. I am offering my humble opinions, hoping that they will be submitted to the conference for public resolution and implementation. I believe that the graduation examinations of schools at all levels in our country have always been held by the schools themselves, which is called the school exam system. As time goes on, the disadvantages have become more and more serious, and the original purpose of education has been gradually lost. Now that the period of political tutelage has just begun, it seems that reforms should be carried out to seek renewal. I, Wu Yourong, dare to offer my humble opinions and present the reasons to the conference for review. Our country has been promoting new education for nearly thirty years, and schools have sprung up everywhere. Education at all levels seems to be developing, but when one examines its content, there are very few who are both excellent in teaching and learning and outstanding in performance, while the majority are just empty signs and perfunctory. What is even worse is that some people run schools for profit and sell diplomas. Those who seek knowledge do so with the diploma as the goal. Teachers and students deceive each other, regardless of their own intelligence, completely losing the meaning of education. This is the first disadvantage of the school exam system. Education at all levels is the foundation for building a society and a country. If graduation is granted indiscriminately without corresponding restrictions, then after graduation, it will not be able to connect with the education at the time of enrollment, or adapt to the needs of society. The graduates will be unable to distinguish between fish and pork, and will be incompetent in any skill. Parents often turn to private schools because their graduated children lack the ability to enter higher education and make a living, or change careers halfway. There are even those in society who see schools as factories for manufacturing vagrants. The belief in new education has completely fallen. This is the second disadvantage of the school exam system. Education at all levels is a factory for shaping the character, intelligence, and physique of young people. If there is no accurate standard, and graduation is granted indiscriminately when the time limit is reached, then under this system, the excellent do not need to work hard, and the inferior have no motivation to improve. Even those who are in charge of education cannot avoid being trapped in the habit of laziness and perfunctoriness. The mechanism for cultivating talents has become a trap for causing harm. If this continues, education will inevitably go bankrupt. This is the third disadvantage of the school exam system. Now, if we want to eliminate the above-mentioned harms, we can only follow the principle of examination advocated by the Premier, order schools at all levels across the country to prepare a list of students who should take the graduation examination, affix photos, and submit them to the county, provincial, and central education authorities for review. Then, the authorities will convene relevant agencies to jointly hire those who are excellent in character and learning and who are deeply familiar with the curriculum standards and educational principles to organize graduation unified examination committees at all levels of schools to hold graduation unified examinations. In this way, the harms can be eliminated, and the benefits are threefold. First, the educational advocacy of our Party can be realized. Reading the declaration of the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Committee, one says that in view of the current situation in China, culture is backward, the economy is backward, and the people's physical and mental health are all weak. The only hope lies in the youth who are rising up. The second says that popularizing national education and raising the people's knowledge to create healthy citizens is the foundation for building the country. The so-called youth who are rising up and the so-called national education refer to the students of today. It is undeniable that education at all levels in our country is not perfect, and students are not receiving perfect education. If we do not invigorate it, then raising the people's knowledge will be empty talk, and the youth who are the only hope will be disappointed. If unified examinations are implemented, then teaching and learning will encourage each other, the level will be comparable, graduation will not be indiscriminate, and our Party's educational advocacy of raising the people's knowledge and creating healthy citizens can be realized. Second, the national education achievements can be accurately investigated. Education at all levels is the foundation for building a healthy society and country. This is the fundamental proposition of our Party to save the country. Those who are responsible for educational administration are all eager to examine it in detail to encourage them. However, the only method of examination is to send supervisors or special commissioners to conduct strict inspections and report the facts. But the inspection time of supervisors and special commissioners is very short, and it is difficult to know all the content. Moreover, the preparations and decorations of both teaching and learning parties have changed their usual attitude. Therefore, what the supervisors and special commissioners can inspect and report may not all be the usual and true achievements. In case the supervisors and special commissioners are not suitable, there is also the malpractice of soliciting and reversing. If unified examinations are implemented, the authenticity of students' achievements, the comparison of school subjects, and the merits and demerits of the heads of each subject can be truly reflected in the unified examination. Based on this, strict rewards and punishments will be imposed, and both teaching and learning parties will feel that there is no escape, and they will all be vigilant and know to work hard. This will not only improve the level, but also tend to be true and consistent. As a result, education at all levels can achieve good results, and a healthy society and country can be built. Third, education policies can be effectively implemented. Educational policies are to respond to the trends of the times and promote the transformation of society. The importance of their relationship is self-evident. If the graduation unified examination is implemented, and the student's achievement, whether it meets the spirit of the policy, is used as the standard for graduation and retention, and as the evaluation of the merits and demerits of the school, then teachers and students will not dare to regard the policy as a mere formality. It will be seen that the competent authority and the school authorities are united, and every policy decision will be an order in the morning and a fact in the evening. This can eliminate the previous malpractices of numbness and indifference, and create a very dynamic and organic group. As said before, the harms are like that, and as said later, the benefits are like this. Therefore, I, Wu Yourong, at the end of the sixteenth year, tried out the graduation unified examination of primary schools in Liancheng County, Fujian, and the results were very effective. In the seventeenth year, no less than twenty counties in Fujian Province followed suit. According to the reports of various counties, they all believed that it was a good way to improve education. The students, their parents, and all sectors of society praised it, and they deeply believed in and admired the graduates who had already taken the unified examination. Even the students were all very happy, thinking that from now on, our new education can wash away the shame of the past that all graduates passed without any ability. I, Wu Yourong, have gone from ideal to belief in graduation unified examinations, from belief to trial, and from trial to good results, and have vigorously promoted them, from one county to more than twenty counties. I hope that after this conference, you will pay special attention to the graduation unified examination, and I urge you to implement the unified examination for the students who should take the graduation examination at the end of the eighteenth year, and continue to carry it out from now on. After ten years of strict examination, education at all levels will surely be

Page 12

First, the scope of American books, compared with the era, is no different from heaven and earth. The country has a sound education to create sound citizens, and the prosperity of the country and the revitalization of the nation will respond like an echo. It can be expected. Do you think that my words are not wrong? I will work hard with you. I am anxious and look forward to it. Wu Yourong, Representative of Overseas Chinese from Taiwan

Henan Education Plan 110

▲Zhang Honglie, Director of Henan Education Department 111

I originally intended to make a very detailed plan for education in Henan, seeking correction from educators. Unfortunately, the political changes were so hurried that the drafts were not completed, which is a regret. Now, I will briefly explain the general idea.

(1) Higher Education: Since 1927, Henan Zhongshan University has opened five departments of liberal arts, science, agriculture, law, and medicine. The number of students in the five departments has reached more than 900, and the funding has reached 370,000 yuan. The quantity can be said to have developed significantly, but the equipment, funding, and professors are not enough to meet the needs. It is planned to stop recruiting preparatory courses this autumn, reduce the number of departments, and concentrate funding, starting with quality, so that the name can match the reality.

(2) Secondary Education: Secondary education in Henan includes 14 provincial junior high schools, 1 senior high school, 5 male normal schools, 2 female normal schools, 1 female middle school, and 4 vocational schools. There are about 40 other county-level junior high schools. Due to repeated changes and unrest, the content is not substantial. It is planned to spend three years reorganizing the interior of the middle school, increasing funding, adding school buildings, books, instruments, and other equipment, and improving teachers' treatment, concentrating teacher talents. After the reorganization plan is completed, it will be expanded.

(3) Primary Education: For primary education in Henan, reorganization and expansion should be carried out simultaneously. In other words, reorganize county and municipal primary schools on the one hand, and train teachers and increase funds on the other, and gradually expand after one year, with the goal of completing universal education.

(4) Adult Remedial Education: For adult illiterate people, it was originally planned to have them receive education in remedial schools within six years. Therefore, the province has established a mass normal school and a mass experimental school to train teachers. All agencies and schools have attached mass schools and vocational training classes as a preliminary plan. In the rural areas, there are mass remedial classes in the classrooms of primary schools every night, and mass schools are set up in public places in each village as a second step plan. Investigate the number of illiterate adults in various places, conduct detailed statistics, and provide remedial education in stages. If there are still people in the locality who have not received remedial education within six years, the person in charge and the person who has not received education will be subject to appropriate penalties. After six years, the people will be able to exercise their powers, so as to facilitate all the work during the period of political tutelage as a final plan.

(5) Social Education: The Education Department has set up a Social Education Promotion Department to manage social education in the province. Each county has established a Social Education Lecture Office to manage social education in the county. The province has established a mass museum, an art college, a sports field, a library, a circulating library, adult mass and agricultural, industrial, and commercial remedial schools, etc. Each county has also been established in order. After the locality is settled, it will be expanded. It is also planned to set up a social education agency in each county to study and implement good methods and train practical talents, so as to complete the mission of social education.

The above are all briefly stated. After the detailed plan is printed, it will be distributed separately. (April 15, 1930, in the capital)

Review Committee of the Compulsory Education Group

Discussion on the Four-Three System for Secondary Schools Wang Maozu 112

▲Reasons 113

1. The German middle school lasts for nine years, and the students graduate at the age of eighteen. The French middle school has a preliminary stage of four years and a later stage of three years, and the graduation age is also seventeen or eighteen. The American middle school implements a three-three system, and the graduation age is eighteen. The Japanese middle school used to be a five-year system. Due to teaching improvement and increased level, it has been changed to four years, plus three years of higher school, for a total of seven years. The graduation age is around twenty. Under the German and French middle schools, there are preparatory classes with a study period of three years and four years respectively. The United States and Japan are promoted from the primary school ladder. Primary schools are mostly six years. Our country imitates the six-three-three system, and the total number of years for primary and secondary schools is twelve, and the graduation age is also eighteen years, which is similar to the schools of various countries and shorter than the school age of Japan. Considering the middle school curriculum of our country, the local language, party doctrine, local history and geography, general social knowledge, and general knowledge of Chinese culture are more burdensome in terms of the relationship on the national culture than the curricula of other countries. It is even more necessary to study foreign languages, general world knowledge, various general sciences, and vocational skills. The difficulty of allocation and the fatigue of students can be imagined. However, if we want to match the study years of European and American middle schools, we will inevitably be blindly imitating. If the level of middle schools cannot be improved, then university education cannot be progressed. In addition to finding ways to improve teaching, it is necessary to extend it by one year because the curriculum is burdensome and must be studied.

2. Curriculum allocation is most difficult in the junior high school stage. Since the promulgation of the new school system in the eleventh year, the debate between the three-three system and the four-two system has not ceased. Even the middle school regulations promulgated by the former University Council also listed the three-three system and the four-two system in parallel. Currently, the junior high school curriculum standards set by the Ministry of Education have a total of 180 credits, with an average of more than 30 credits per semester. I am afraid that it is not suitable for children's ability to understand and digest, and only 12 credits are given to history and geography, and 15 credits are given to natural sciences, including geology, minerals, meteorology, etc. I am afraid that there will be many obstacles in actual teaching. If junior high school is only prepared for entering higher education, a six-year consistent system can be established from high school. However, if junior high school becomes a separate stage, then the elements of modern world culture and general science teaching materials must also form a circle, but the content of this circle is very thin, which in turn reduces the level of senior high school. This is one of the problems. Moreover, in theory, it is stipulated that one hour of class and one hour of self-study is one credit. In practice, students often spend two or three hours preparing for the basic subjects, and they inevitably neglect the other subjects. This is the second problem. Primary schools use pure Mandarin, while junior high schools must understand classical Chinese and be able to write classical Chinese. In the future, entering higher education and application cannot completely abolish classical Chinese. Therefore, a gap has already occurred between primary school and junior high school, and junior high school Chinese language teaching is more difficult than before. Considering that the school age of middle schools in Germany and France is advanced, it is mainly because the basic teaching subjects, language training, are different from ordinary primary schools. This is a dual-track school system, which is contrary to the trend of modern popularization. It would be very good if junior high schools in our country can train students who are preparing to enter higher education and those who are preparing for vocational careers separately. However, according to the curriculum standards set by the Ministry of Education, vocational courses only have 5 to 15 credits. It is difficult to achieve the effect of practical application. This is the third problem. According to the various difficulties mentioned above, it is especially necessary to increase the time limit.

3. Since the promulgation of the new school system in the eleventh year, the middle schools with four-year system in various places have been eager to run high schools as if the higher vocational schools have been enthusiastically changed to universities, regardless of the economic situation, equipment, and teacher qualifications. The content of the school is empty and the teaching level has not been improved. It is better to run a four-year middle school diligently and realistically. However, after implementing the three-three system, if we want to shorten it by one year and change it to run a junior high school, then we will be depressed. Local people also take pride in changing to a high school and promote it together, regardless of how many students can enter the high school. Therefore, more high schools are set up, and the efficiency of education is diluted due to division. This is also a problem with extremely valuable research value. If the four-three system is adopted, the Ministry of Education should send personnel to cooperate with the Education Department to investigate the educational conditions of the areas where middle schools in each province are located, the school performance, the number of students, the school building equipment, the teacher's academic qualifications, experience, writings, etc., and set a standard for each. Each province divides the senior high school areas, merges those that should be merged, and adds those that should be added. If training is concentrated in this way, it is not difficult to increase the efficiency of education.

4. Junior high schools should be universal, and senior high schools should be selected. Some people think that after extending the time limit by one year, they are afraid that the economic power of education cannot bear it. This can be solved by scholarships. If it is like today's system, junior high schools already have the sigh of the palace wall, let alone senior high schools. The establishment of junior high schools has theoretical aspects that belong to psychology, and social aspects, which are very long. It is also important to explore personality and implement vocational training. If one year is added, then vocational training will not be worried about being young, and more opportunities can be given to practice it. When they come out and apply it, their skills will be improved, and their sense of responsibility will be more abundant. Moreover, at the beginning of the implementation of compulsory education, Jiangsu Province alone lacks about 14,000 teachers in the first year. If the third-year students of junior high school volunteer to be teachers, they can choose to study education courses, and in the second semester of the fourth year, they can be assigned to practice, which can supplement the lack of teachers. Since the previous junior high school graduates, in addition to entering higher education, mostly stay at home idly, and are at a loss, which is a major concern in education and society. (It is easier to find ways for senior high school graduates who do not enter higher education)

5. According to the experience of various middle schools in Jiangsu Province, about 80% of junior high school graduates enter higher education, and many drop out within one year after entering senior high school. Then, adding one year to junior high school to enrich general subjects and add vocational training is also to meet the needs of society. The underdeveloped provinces in senior high school also have four-year junior high schools, which can also improve the level of education. According to the above, after the middle school is changed to the four-three system, there are about several benefits: (1) The curriculum is easier to allocate; (2) Vocational training is easier to implement; (3) Senior high schools can be managed in a concentrated manner, increasing efficiency; (4) The level of university is improved accordingly. Is it appropriate? I would like to discuss it with educators.

Essay

A Little Hope for the Second National Education Conference Ma He-tian 114

The Second National Education Conference has opened. The special features of this time are,

as Minister Jiang said at the opening ceremony, (1) that the entire systematic plan for improving national education was formulated in advance by experts, planning for twenty years, so as to avoid piecemeal and chaotic proposals based on subjective views, regardless of urgency, and (2) that the members are required to have education administrators from each county and city, one from each province, who know the actual situation of each place. This is really the advantage of this conference over the first one.

But I still have a little doubt. (1) China has too large an area, and the cultural level, economic situation, and various special circumstances of each place are too different. I don't know if a unified and consistent plan can be suitable. (2) The plan must be based on facts, that is, based on the investigation and statistics of each place. The situation in various parts of our country is too complicated. There are many places where all investigation and statistical materials are absolutely absent. Some have a part, but they are not accurate. Is it appropriate to base an inaccurate or unfounded plan on the actual situation and can it be implemented? Moreover, in the current situation, there are drastic and irregular changes in various places almost every year. Is there a risk that the twenty-year plan will be wrong in one place and wrong in the whole plan? (3) What percentage of the education administrators of each county and city actually attended this time? What percentage of those who really seek from the people? Moreover, the circumstances vary greatly from place to place. Can one person represent them? Is the result still separated from the real situation in each place? Therefore, I hope that this conference will consider the special circumstances of each place in various plans and measures, so as to have a retractable flexibility, and leave room for active and flexible changes in the whole, so that the personnel who are actually responsible for the education administration of each place can implement it according to the environment, so that the plan does not deviate from the facts, and does not "put it on the shelf" as a result of the first conference.

Reflections on Improving Preliminary Education Plans in the Education Program - Dongqing 115

Primary education is mostly run by local municipalities and counties. The social conditions of each municipality and county are naturally vastly different, each with its own characteristics and difficulties. In running elementary school education, one must pay attention to the individuality of children on the one hand, and adapt to the local social conditions on the other. This is something everyone knows and acknowledges. Therefore, some may think it impossible to stipulate an improvement plan in the education program that can suit the actual conditions of all municipalities and counties across the country.

Indeed, it is impossible to set a method that is completely suitable for all municipalities and counties across the country. Not only is it theoretically impossible to imagine, but it has also been definitively proven to be impossible in practice. Since the Qing Dynasty's reform and establishment of schools, the government has revised [educational regulations] several times. The previous government also formulated and promulgated many regulations and bylaws for administering elementary schools in municipalities and counties across the country. But, I ask, what effect have these past rules and regulations had on the teachers who actually run elementary schools in municipalities and counties?

In good organizations or elementary schools, rules and regulations are always felt to be obstacles to progress, shackles that bind experimentation and research. In bad organizations or elementary schools, they are merely followed as routine, or even outwardly obeyed but inwardly violated, only put on a show when inspectors arrive. When formulating methods, people often only consider how to prevent malfeasance and how to crack down, focusing mostly on the negative aspects. As a result, the negative measures fail to make the greedy, lazy, and corrupt know how to improve, but instead severely restrict those who are able to progress automatically and have a spirit of experimentation. This not only proves that it is impossible but can also be summed up simply and directly in one sentence: "It's unnecessary!"

If it's impossible and unnecessary, why waste sixteen and a half pages of paper to occupy a chapter in the national education program?

Originally, things in the world change; they are not fixed. Statistics tell us that it is impossible to find absolutely identical and equal things, whether in material or human affairs. How can we manage ever-changing things with a rigid and uniform method? However, we humans have a special ability to find the unchanging amidst the changing. The objects and facts obtained from statistics are all changing. However, the principles found in statistics can summarize many changing phenomena into several unchanging formulas. The method of running elementary schools should vary according to the social conditions of each municipality and county. How to deal with this change, how to cope with this change, can be based on facts and refer to the successes and failures of others. [Photo of Guanghua, member of the Secondary Education Review Committee, inserted here.] Find some formulas or things like formula principles. Therefore, I say that the primary education part of the education program should focus on this point.

The education program can also be said to be a more detailed design in administration. Educational administration should be carried out using educational methods. This is also a recent trend. This is not empty theory; others have already tried it and achieved considerable success. Educational methods are not rigid, nor are they uniform, but neither are they unsystematic and random. We all know that teachers need to have lesson plans with outlines when teaching, and schools need to have predetermined plans when handling affairs. Handling educational administration is also like a kind of educational function, so naturally, there can also be a predetermined plan for proceeding, and this plan should not be imposed but guided. Therefore, the plan regarding the primary education part of the education program should also focus on this point.

If these two points can be found, the primary education part of the program may have some practical results in the future. This is my personal hope.

▲ Inspections begin today

▲ Approximately 5,000 participants

He Yingqin, Commander of the Boy Scouts of China

▲ Temporary First Aid Matters

During the scout inspection, temporary first aid matters are originally stipulated to be the responsibility of the Health Section of the local area. Due to the large number of personnel participating in the inspection, the office has informed the Central Model Hospital regarding temporary emergency matters. The Health Section of this office will provide treatment, and those who are more seriously ill and need to be hospitalized will be sent directly to the hospital. At the same time, two doctors will be hired by the office to be responsible for temporary first aid work, and a large number of medicines will be prepared for use.

▲ Grand Camp Held Yesterday

The Grand Camp of the All-Scout General Inspection was delayed due to continuous rain for several days. The sky cleared on the 16th. On the morning of the 17th, after Dai strongly advocated for it, it was decided that the Grand Camp would still be held at Xiaoying from that day. Starting at 2:00 PM, they departed from the officer research class, and the management section distributed campsites. Instantly, hundreds of tents were set up. Looking at the grand scene of the field camp from a high place, one couldn't help but feel refreshed. In the evening, the camp lights were lit, and the candlelight shone brightly. After dinner, each group either gathered for a high-spirited conversation, visited each other, played harmonicas and sang songs, or performed and showed off their skills. All the scouts were also full of vigor. It was a grand spectacle unprecedented in the history of the Boy Scouts of China, a lively scene of nature.

▲ General Inspection Ceremony

The General Inspection Ceremony of All Scouts has been revised as follows due to He Yingqin's departure to the front and the inability to hold a supplementary oath: (1) Music; (2) All stand at attention; (3) Sing the Party Song; (4) Raise the flag; (5) Music; (6) Bow three times to the Party, National Flag, and the portrait of Dr. Sun Yat-sen; (7) The Chairman respectfully reads Dr. Sun Yat-sen's will; (8) Three minutes of silence; (9) Hold the General Inspection, music; (A) Parade: 1. Report the number of people, 2. Inspection, 3. Basic Exercises; (B) Marching: 1. Command to start, 2. The whole group circles the field once, 3. Speech, 4. Cheers, 5. Music, 6. Return to camp.

Zou Fan, a member of the Central Committee, was additionally appointed as a judge for the All-Scout General Inspection.

The Central Training Department has prepared various prizes to be awarded to the scouts participating in the inspection to encourage them. The prizes include 19 satin flags, 8 silver shields, and Dr. Sun Yat-sen's calligraphy. It is planned to issue one copy to each group as a souvenir. In addition, each group will be presented with a photo of He Yingqin.

▲ Notify All Sectors to Visit

The Beijing City Party Department Civil Training Committee notified all schools and mass organizations in Beijing to visit. In addition, all students of the Central Political School will also arrive at that time.

▲ Jimei and Other Schools Rush to Make Clothing

The Boy Scout Headquarters stipulated that all scout uniforms that are self-made will not be allowed to enter the field. It is now heard that the scout leaders of Jimei, Guangzhao, Jinan, Jiangnvzhuan, and other schools are most heartbroken by the inability to participate in the general inspection. On the one hand, they are urging workers to rush to make them, and on the other hand, they are borrowing clothes everywhere. They may not be disappointed at the time.

▲ Yesterday's Rehearsal Inspection

In order to achieve a neat form for the inspection on the 18th, the office held a rehearsal at the inspection site at 2:00 PM yesterday. At that time, the management section sent scouts to ask the public to leave the field so that the performance could be carried out. Most of the audience was reluctant to leave. After the scouts persuaded them in many ways, they slowly dispersed. Outside the field, the scouts were able to begin preparations. The office convened the group leaders for a discussion, and then convened the deputy commanders and division commanders to explain the key points of the rehearsal. After the explanation, each group gathered around the group station. The office convened the group leaders for a second discussion. After the discussion, the office director Shi Weihuan, deputy director Zhang Zhongren, and member of the Central Committee Zhang Daofan inspected the field in a car. The military appearance was quite orderly. After the inspection, the drill of the march-past and basic movements began. The maneuvers were very beautiful. After the march-past, the marching drill was immediately followed. The entire scout group marched around the field for several weeks. The neat steps and graceful posture won a lot of praise from the audience, and the applause was like thunder. However, because of the continuous rain in the previous days, although it cleared on the 16th, there was still standing water in the field. The scouts felt great difficulty when passing through the area. The office decided to fill the field with great difficulty that night to facilitate the inspection on the 18th. After the marching drill, they lined up in front of the inspection platform to listen to the speech, but due to time constraints, the speech was omitted. Then, the whole group shouted the slogans "Long live the Boy Scouts of China," "Long live the Chinese Kuomintang," and "Long live the Chinese Republic." Each dispersed and returned to the camp area. It was already 6:00 PM.

Important Announcements from the Office 117

▲ A Brief History of the Boy Scouts

▲ The Significance of Holding the General Inspection

The office issued a brief history of the Boy Scouts and the significance of holding the National Boy Scout General Inspection. (1) The Establishment of the World Boy Scouts: Boy Scout training began at the end of the 19th century. The first World Boy Scout group was established in the summer of 1907. The founder was Mr. Baden-Powell of England. His intention was to cultivate hardworking and self-reliant young children to correct the bad habits and abuses of laziness and reliance, and to instill an inner mission, such as the British Boy Scouts' instillation of loyalty to the royal family and respect for God. (2) The Establishment of the Boy Scouts in Our Country: The Boy Scout cause in our country began in the first year of the Republic, organized by Wuchang Wenhua University. Later, various places followed suit, especially church schools. The shortcomings were: 1. The organization was uneven, with each going its own way; 2. The training only imitated the superficialities of Europe and America, without real meaning, and even became a tool for cultural aggression by imperialism. (3) The Past of the Kuomintang Boy Scouts: Our Party is deeply concerned about the youth and children of the country. Therefore, in the 15th year of the Republic, the Kuomintang Boy Scout Committee was established. Later, due to the focus on the Northern Expedition and other work, not much could be done in this regard. (4) In May of the 17th year of the Republic, the Central Training Department proposed amendments to the Party Boy Scout Regulations, etc., which were passed by the Standing Committee. Under the Central Training Department, the Party Boy Scout Headquarters was established to handle organization, training, compilation, review, and assessment. For more than a year, the results have been quite remarkable. (5) The Renaming and Reorganization of the Boy Scouts of China: After the Third Plenary Session, the Central Government planned to further reorganize the Boy Scout cause, renamed it the Boy Scouts of China, and established the Boy Scout Headquarters of China, directly under the Central Executive Committee, and established the Boy Scout Education Section under the Training Department. (6) The Current Situation of the Boy Scouts of China: Since the establishment of the Party Boy Scout Headquarters until now, the Boy Scouts in various places have developed rapidly under the leadership of our Party. The total number of Boy Scouts who have been registered is about 200 groups, with more than 13,300 people. There are more than 1,100 service members. More than a dozen Boy Scout social organizations have applied for registration. This is a very good phenomenon. (7) The Postponement of the General Inspection: This National General Inspection and Grand Camp is an unprecedented initiative in our country. It was originally scheduled to be held on the Double Tenth Festival last year. Later, due to the short time frame, it was feared that the distant regions would not be able to participate, so it was changed to be held today. The Boy Scouts and service members who attended are not afraid of hardship and have come from afar, which is deeply gratifying. (8) The Significance of the General Inspection: The significance of the General Inspection is: 1. To understand the achievements of past management; 2. To serve as a reference for future progress; 3. To make the Boy Scout situation known to the whole society and receive assistance; 4. To allow the Boy Scouts and service members from various places to connect with each other, foster friendship, and enhance academics; 5. To commemorate the anniversary of our Party establishing its capital in Nanjing, holding the General Inspection in the capital, the Boy Scouts from various places should be more aware of the importance of their mission and resolutely take on the responsibility and actively do it. (9) The Meaning of Re-Inspection: Especially in the daily efforts of the Boy Scouts after the event. It is hoped that the Boy Scouts and service members in various places will understand this and strive forward every day.

Shanghai Student Federation Opposes the Screening of Humiliating Films by Ginling College 120

The Shanghai Special Municipality Student Federation sent a telegram to the nation yesterday, opposing the screening of films insulting to the Chinese people at the Christian Education Annual Meeting of Ginling College. The telegram stated (excerpt): It is observed that imperialists use Christianity as a tool for cultural aggression, using every means to numb the youth of our country. Recently, they have intensified their efforts unscrupulously. The Christian Youth Association of Ginling College even screened films made by Professor Hsu Fu-erh himself at the entertainment gathering, depicting the slums of our country, snotty-nosed children, (women with bound feet, monks conducting funerals, beggars picking lice, and various other ugly scenes). Such open screenings are intentionally insulting. If we do not strongly oppose this and instead passively accept it, we, the descendants of the Yellow Emperor, would truly be ignorant of human shame. Our Federation has long been deeply concerned about the cultural aggression of Christianity and the numbing of youth by youth associations in various regions. We are even more indignant about the screening of films insulting to the Chinese people by the Ginling College Youth Association. We earnestly hope that compatriots across the country will unite in opposition, further prevent cultural aggression, and diligently recover educational rights. This would be a great blessing for the future of the nation. We respectfully submit this telegram for your wise consideration. Shanghai Special Municipality Student Union Executive Committee, [Official Seal] (National Society)

Elementary Education Group Review Committee

Jinan University Schedules Comfort for Athletes 125

The Shanghai Special Municipality won the overall championship at the National Games this time. Most of the athletes came from Jinan University, who were the backbone of the team. Taking Cao Yu alone as an example, he scored 22 points in the all-around competition, accounting for two-thirds of the Shanghai team's total score and one-quarter of the overall conference score. In track and field, he scored 15 points, accounting for one-third of Shanghai's total score. Others such as Zhong Lianji and Hao Chunde from the track and field team, and Dai Linjing, Feng Yunyou, Wen Guanmao, Chen Jiaqiu, Jiang Shanjing, Zhuang Shihong, and Lin Songfa from the football team were all prominent figures who made a resounding impact. Nearly 30 male and female athletes participated. Recognizing that these students were able to bring glory to Shanghai, the school authorities decided to hold a comfort meeting on the morning of the 25th of this month, with plenty of refreshments. In addition to the championship trophy won by the overall team being stored in the Education Bureau of the Special Municipality, the prizes won by each athlete, totaling dozens, have been on display in the western section of the Hongnian Library building since yesterday, open to the public. Among the most valuable items are the silver pavilion presented by President Chiang for the first place in the decathlon, engraved with "Fraternity and Sincerity," the silver cup from the Fujian Provincial Government, engraved with surpassing talents, the silver cup presented by Lu Diping, Chairman of the Jiangxi Provincial Government, a Chinese Bookstore Four Histories subscription voucher (priced at 280 yuan, subscription price 140 yuan), a gold medal, the silver cup presented by President Chiang for first place in the pentathlon, engraved with diligence, courage, faith, and loyalty, the silver goblet from Lin Yunhai, Mayor of Guangzhou Special Municipality, five embroidered eagles, pines and cranes, and horizontal panels from He Jian, Chairman of the Hunan Provincial Government, first place in the long jump, a silver shield presented by the Suiyuan Provincial Government, engraved with the light of the nation, second place in the men's 100 meters, a silver shield presented by the Henan Provincial Government, engraved with self-improvement, and another engraved with a strong country and a strong race. Other items include a refined landscape mirror screen made by Du Jinsheng, and silver shields, silver screens, silver cups, fountain pens, etc., a dazzling array of beautiful items. In addition, the school holds an annual Spring Sports Meet, which is scheduled to be held next Friday and Saturday. Preparations are actively underway, and there will surely be a grand occasion at that time.

Today is the 3rd Anniversary of the National Government Establishing its Capital in Nanjing 131

▲The Municipal Executive Committee Holds a Celebration Meeting

▲To be Held at Penglai Grand Theater at 9:00 AM

Today (the 18th) is the 3rd anniversary of the National Government establishing its capital in Nanjing. Stalemate on the Issue of Chinese Directors at the Shanghai Municipal Council 132

▲ Chinese Ratepayers' Association Held an Emergency Meeting Yesterday

▲ Japanese Residents' Representatives Express Sympathy for Our Chinese People

▲ Shanghai Municipal Council to Convene a Special Meeting of Westerners

The General Assembly of the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the International Settlement convened a temporary emergency meeting yesterday afternoon at the Chamber of Commerce to discuss the issue of Chinese directors at the Shanghai Municipal Council. After two hours of discussion, it was resolved that the resolution of the Western ratepayers' annual meeting regarding Chinese directors was invalid. At the same time, three representatives were publicly elected to go to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to lodge a serious protest. The newly elected five Chinese directors insisted on attending the meetings of the Municipal Council. If the Municipal Council only allows three Chinese directors to attend, then other countermeasures will be decided upon. On the Municipal Council's side, it must abide by the resolutions of the Western ratepayers' annual meeting, making its situation very difficult. Therefore, the issue has largely reached a stalemate. The details of what was heard yesterday are as follows:

▲ Results of the Emergency Meeting: General Assembly of the Chinese Ratepayers' Association

Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, the General Assembly of the Chinese Ratepayers' Association held a temporary emergency meeting at the standing committee room of the Chamber of Commerce. Over fifty people attended, chaired by Wang Xiaolai, who reported on the purpose of the meeting. Yu Qiaqing reported on the history of struggles to increase the number of Chinese directors and the methods of not recognizing the Western ratepayers' decision on the rights of Chinese ratepayers were discussed. The following resolutions were unanimously passed: (1) Publish a declaration in the newspaper stating that the Western Ratepayers' Association has no right to decide on the issue of Chinese directors of the Chinese Ratepayers' Association. (2) Refute the arguments of the British lawyer Macdonell, to be drafted by the secretary of the General Assembly, and revised and published by the chairman of the General Assembly in conjunction with the Chinese directors committee. (3) Telegraph to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs requesting serious negotiations, and appoint Wang Xiaolai, Yu Qiaqing, and Hu Mengjia to petition the Ministry.

▲ Declaration of the Ratepayers' Association: The Shanghai International Settlement Chinese Ratepayers'

Association declares: This Association affirms that the Shanghai International Settlement Western Ratepayers' Association has no right to discuss the civic rights that the Chinese ratepayers of the Shanghai International Settlement should have. Based on this principle, the rejection of the motion to increase the number of Chinese directors in the Shanghai Municipal Council by two at the Western Ratepayers' meeting on April 16th of this year is naturally invalid. This is solemnly declared.

▲ Letter from the Municipal Council: After the Association held its General Assembly the day before yesterday and elected the Chinese directors committee and the executive committee, in addition to sending letters to the elected candidates to notify the various groups and organizations, it also formally notified the Board of Directors of the Shanghai Municipal Council. The original letter stated: To Mr. Macnaghten, Chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Council: Regarding the directors representing the Chinese ratepayers within the Settlement to attend your council's executive affairs from 1920 to the end of 1931, we have followed the instructions of the Executive Yuan's Ministry of Foreign Affairs of our national government, and have received a note from the Spanish Minister to China, approving the increase from three seats to five seats. On April 16th, the General Assembly of this Association elected Mr. Yuan Ludeng, Mr. Yu Qiaqing, Mr. Xu Xinliu, Mr. Bei Songsun, and Mr. Liu Hongsheng to serve as directors. The six committee members elected were Mr. Lin Kanghou, Mr. Tai Runqing, Mr. Chen Tingrui, Mr. Li Fuxun, Mr. Qian Longzhang, and Mr. Wu Yunzhai. We are enclosing the resumes of the directors and committee members for your reference. Sincerely, Chairman Wang Xiaolai, Xu Jilong, April 17, 1930, Republic of China. Attached: one copy of the resumes of the directors and committee members.

▲ Foreign Directors Assumed Office Yesterday: The nine foreign directors of the Municipal Council, six British, two Japanese, and one American, all assumed office yesterday afternoon at the Municipal Council. However, the Chinese directors did not go because they had not received notification from the Municipal Council's office. The nine foreign directors, as in past years, elected the chairman and vice-chairman, unanimously electing Macnaghten as chairman and Hebar as vice-chairman. Regarding the process of rejecting the increase of two Chinese director seats, there is a fact that is quite interesting, and it is specially noted here. Only 252 people attended the Western Ratepayers' Annual Meeting the day before yesterday. Because the annual meeting has no quorum requirement, it can still be held as usual even if only one or two people attend. Macdonell, the mover of the motion against increasing the number of Chinese directors, is a lawyer who was originally recuperating at the Hong En Hospital. Unexpectedly, he suddenly attended and gave a speech, causing a great uproar, from which the matter arose. Many of the Westerners who raised their hands to reject the motion regretted it afterward.

▲ Attitude of the Municipal Council: Yesterday, this newspaper's reporter visited Mr. Edward, the Secretary-General of the Municipal Council, to inquire about the Municipal Council's position and its solutions to the issue. Mr. Edward replied that all the foreign directors of the Municipal Council, as well as the Director-General Fessenden and he, were genuinely sincere in proposing the increase of Chinese directors from three to five seats in order to achieve Chinese-foreign cooperation. The Municipal Council was confident that the proposal would be passed smoothly at the Western Ratepayers' Annual Meeting, but the result was unexpectedly rejected. The Municipal Council is very sorry that things did not go as planned. Furthermore, because the Western Ratepayers' Association is the master of the Municipal Council, the Municipal Council has no choice but to comply with the resolutions of the Association. Therefore, the twists and turns of this issue are not the fault of the Municipal Council, and it hopes that the Chinese side will forgive it and not punish the Municipal Council for this. At the meeting this afternoon, all the directors unanimously expressed regret over this unfortunate event. As a temporary compromise, they only hope that the three Chinese directors who received the most votes among the newly elected five Chinese directors will attend the Municipal Council as usual. The three gentlemen are the original directors, and have a good relationship with the Municipal Council through years of cooperation. The Municipal Council very much welcomes their attendance. If, as reported, the five Chinese directors insist on attending at the same time, or else all of them will be absent, then the Municipal Council will have no Chinese directors this year, and Chinese-foreign cooperation will return to the situation of five years ago. Another report states that foreign residents in Shanghai are very dissatisfied that one person spoke out against the proposal at that time, and the voters did not review it carefully, and hastily rejected it. In order to comply with public opinion, the Municipal Council plans to convene a special meeting of Western ratepayers within days to reconsider the case, so that a thorough discussion can be made, and the original purpose can be achieved.

▲ Special Meeting of Westerners: Subsequently, the reporter visited Deputy Director-General Jones and asked about the temporary convening of a special meeting of Western ratepayers to re-vote on the case. Jones replied that this matter was originally the only remedy at present. However, based on his past experience, he felt that it was quite difficult to convene. Because the Western Ratepayers' Annual Meeting has no quorum requirement, it is only necessary for twenty-five people to propose convening a special meeting, which can be done. However, there is still a quorum requirement, that is, more than one-third of the foreign ratepayers must attend to hold the meeting. There are about three thousand foreign taxpayers in the city. If one-third is used as a quorum, then more than one thousand people must attend. In 1925, the Municipal Council wanted to convene a special meeting to deal with the issue of child labor, but it failed. Since then, the Municipal Council has repeatedly wanted to amend the regulations, but has repeatedly failed to do so. Therefore, it is still uncertain whether it can be held this time.

▲ Speech by Mr. Shigemitsu: The Japanese Deputy Minister Shigemitsu, the Japanese directors of the Municipal Council Fukushima and Saito, and representatives of the Japanese Chamber of Commerce, etc., also discussed the issue for several hours at the Japanese Consulate General in Shanghai yesterday, and have discussed concrete solutions. In general, they sympathize with our side, and will express their assistance within days. Mr. Shigemitsu also made a speech for this yesterday, saying, "The proposal to increase the number of Chinese directors in the Shanghai International Settlement Municipal Council from three to five has long been approved by the entire City Council. I believe that this move is appropriate and the most just measure, and I express my extreme approval. I also know that the Japanese residents of Shanghai also agree with this move. Because I have received reports that the Japanese who attended the Western Ratepayers' Meeting yesterday all supported the proposal to increase the number of Chinese directors. The result of the Western Ratepayers' Meeting yesterday was such that I think that a motion opposing the original proposal was suddenly put forward, resulting in a lack of thorough deliberation. I think that for this kind of proposal that is a major issue in the administration of the entire Shanghai, it should be decided after a full debate between the pros and cons. As the acting minister and consul general, I will carefully consider it and strive to seek appropriate measures. I very much hope that the final outcome can realize the most just decision of the City Council. This is not only my personal opinion, but also the representative opinion of the Japanese residents."

▲ Statement by the Japanese Directors: The Japanese directors of the Municipal Council, Fukushima and Saito, came to this newspaper yesterday and stated on behalf of all the Japanese taxpayers that the Japanese have always strongly supported the proposal to increase the number of Chinese director seats, but because there are quite a few people who are not familiar with English, not many attended the ratepayers' annual meeting the day before yesterday, resulting in the sudden rejection of the proposal to increase the number of Chinese director seats. They all expressed regret. As for this newspaper's report yesterday that the rejection of the proposal was due to the manipulation of the Japanese, it was actually a rumor.

▲ Declarations by Various Party Branches: The third and sixth district party branches of this city also issued declarations yesterday. The original text is recorded as follows: (1) Declaration of the Third District Party Branch: It is a common demand of citizens in European and American countries that there should be no representation without taxation, and it is also based on the principle of equality of rights and obligations. More than 80% of our Chinese citizens reside in the Shanghai International Settlement, and the taxes paid account for 60% of the total amount, but the number of Chinese director seats is less than one-fourth. According to the principle of equality of taxation, it is greatly disproportionate. This year, based on the verbal agreement to increase the extra surtax by two, and through repeated negotiations by the diplomatic authorities and the Chinese directors, there was a result of increasing the number of Chinese director seats by two, which is not enough to satisfy our wishes, nor can it achieve the goal of fairness. However, the Western Ratepayers' Meeting yesterday actually rejected it, and lawyer Macdonell even made insulting remarks to our Chinese people. This not only abandoned its credibility, but also showed contempt for our compatriots. Moreover, it is extremely absurd that the number of Chinese director seats for citizens who pay the same taxes should be decided by the Western Ratepayers' Meeting. This district party branch vows to oppose it to the death, and hopes that all compatriots will uphold the spirit of perseverance and work together for the movement to recover the concessions, in order to seek a permanent solution. This is hereby declared. (2) Declaration of the Sixth District Party Branch: (The title is omitted) The proposal to increase the number of Chinese director seats was actually rejected by the Western Ratepayers' Meeting. This is a natural result of seeking cooperation with a tiger, and it is not surprising. However, the concessions are our country's territory. Before the color is changed, the ultimate sovereignty can only belong to the Chinese and not to the Westerners. Since it does not belong to the Westerners, then according to the fair principle of taxation, we should increase the number of Chinese directors to more than twelve in order to conform to the principle of equality of rights and obligations. Now that they have violated the purpose of municipal administration, and they are not willing to accept even the trivial two powerless Chinese director seats, this is not only a contempt for our national sovereignty, but also a trampling on the face of our Chinese nation, and giving us a major embarrassment. Therefore, we dare to demand, under serious protest, that a group of Chinese directors refuse to cooperate with the Westerners, and that the citizens of the entire city declare a rent strike, in order to accommodate our minimum conditions. At the same time, we also hope that the diplomatic authorities will immediately propose negotiations to recover the concessions, so that the area where sovereignty has been lost may have a day of recovery. The members of this association only know how to complete revolutionary diplomacy, abolish unequal treaties, in order to achieve the goal of coexistence and co-prosperity. If anyone dares to obstruct our plan, or invade our land and become long-term occupants, we vow to bomb it with ten thousand dan of neck blood. This is hereby declared. We look forward to a response. (The rest is omitted)

▲ Report in a Western Newspaper: The Da Wan Bao said, "The speech made by a certain gentleman at the City Hall yesterday (16th) against increasing the number of Chinese directors in the Municipal Council, which led to the rejection of the proposal, any reader who reads it will come to a conclusion from their heart, saying, 'It directly regards the Chinese as outsiders, and regards foreigners, i.e., British, American, Japanese, etc. residents, as natives.' Those who regard themselves as natives will naturally regard themselves as heirs to the British Empire's legacy created by Wellington and Mac荣." This kind of reasoning is obviously flawed and dangerous to non-British people. Today's critics of the authorities believe that foreign residents in Shanghai know more about the methods of governing this complex city, and those who are in charge of governing the country should follow the will of the local residents without interference. This policy is harmful and useless. The biggest problem in Shanghai today is that it often has such remarks and tries to implement them. Shanghai's municipal administration should be handled by suitable talents, and should not fall into the hands of those who reside in Shanghai solely for their own personal interests. Those who are far away are clear, and those who are near are obscured. For conflicting foreign interests, the further away those who handle them are, the more fair the judgment and the more clear the views. Last year, there were many achievements in the concessions due to the friendship between China and foreign countries, and there are many future achievements as well. However, a speech at the City Hall and the results it caused have overthrown everything in one night, and even jeopardized the basis of cooperation that has been sought for many years. Increasing two Chinese directors in the Board of Directors has gains and no losses. The gains can not only generate a more friendly and cooperative relationship among these complex ethnic groups, but also open a way to finally resolve the concession issue. Today, the final solution depends entirely on increasing the administrative talent of the Chinese. No one can deny this. It is fundamentally bad that 242 taxpayers who attend the meeting cast 414 votes. No matter how good the administrative of the municipal administration it creates, it cannot hide the flaws in the concession's administrative system, which has long been unable to represent its residents and has lost its fairness. Fortunately, experts are in Shanghai carefully investigating and suggesting remedies, but if there had not been a setback at yesterday's City Hall meeting, the results of the expert investigation would have been easier to accept. In short, foreign residents in Shanghai are ultimately from other countries. If you want to strongly refer to the Chinese people living in the local area as foreigners, and recognize the foreigners who gather at the City Hall as natives, then the fundamental is already wrong.

Central Mint Hosted a Tour for the Press Yesterday 133

▲ Can Mint 400,000 Silver Dollars in Ten Hours

▲ Will Officially Start Minting Upon Receipt of Instructions from the Ministry of Finance

The Central Mint hosted reporters from Chinese and foreign newspapers at its factory site on Xiaoshadu Road at 2:30 PM yesterday. The reporters were led on a tour of various locations by Factory Director Guo Biao, Deputy Factory Director Wei Xianzhang, technicians Tang Xuping, Wen Zongyu, Guo Huide, and American technician H.W. Heard. They bid farewell around 4:00 PM. According to Deputy Factory Director Wei's statement to this newspaper's reporter, all of the factory's machinery is the latest model, and it can mint more than 400,000 silver dollars and more than 200,000 subsidiary coins in ten hours. The model is planned to be adopted from Italy, but it has not been fully determined yet. The fineness of the silver dollar may need to be slightly changed due to the change to the gold standard. At present, all the machinery has been installed, and the workers have also been trained. Minting will begin upon receipt of instructions from the Ministry of Finance. There are currently dozens of workers, and this will be increased to more than 300 after minting officially begins. The National Government has decided to implement the abolition of taels for dollars in July, so it is necessary to mint a sufficient quantity of silver dollars before then. It is expected that the date of commencement of minting is not far away.

▲ History of the Factory: The Central Mint was originally named the Shanghai Mint. When Zhou Ziqi was Minister of Finance in the ninth year of the Republic of China, he commissioned Zhong Wenyao to borrow a large sum from the Shanghai Chinese Banking Group to plan and proceed. After Zhong resigned, the Ministry of Finance commissioned Sa Tongsun to take over and continue the work. At that time, Sa had already purchased and built the address and factory buildings, and various machines had also been ordered from the United States. By the eleventh year, the machines that had been ordered had arrived in Shanghai one after another. The Ministry of Finance did not extract them because the price had not been paid, and the factory was thus stalled. In the twelfth year, the Ministry of Finance commissioned Zhu Youji to take over again, but Zhu resigned not long after. After Zhu left, the Chinese Banking Group took over for safekeeping. In the fourteenth year, Sun Chuanfang arrived in Ning and commissioned Fu Zongyao as the factory director, but he did not take office. In the sixteenth year, the Ministry of Finance of the National Government commissioned Wang Chengzulai to head this factory. After Wang resigned, in the seventeenth year, Tang Shoumin was commissioned to take over again. Not long after, Tang resigned due to the inability to attend to many affairs. In November of the same year, Minister Song of the Ministry of Finance commissioned Guo Biao to take over. In July of the following year, Wei Xianzhang was appointed as deputy factory director to actively carry out the project. The Central Mint has a very large debt. After the two factory directors Guo and Wei took office, they successively petitioned the Ministry of Finance to pay off the debt. Now the surrounding walls, wharf, bridges, dormitory buildings have all been completed, and the coin minting, gas, and electricity machinery have also been installed. They are now being tested separately, and the results are very good.

▲ A Glimpse of the Interior: Yesterday afternoon, reporters from various newspapers first visited the chemical analysis room, which has a row of American-style gas silver melting furnaces, which melt raw silver and then analyze its composition in detail. Next to the chemical analysis room is the raw silver vault. The adjacent room is equipped with multiple silver bar making machines, which crush the raw silver and then make it into silver bars, which are then placed in a sulfuric acid solution and stored in the silver bar vault in the third room. The next is the flattening machine, which flattens the silver bars and then puts them into the silver cake making machine to turn them into cakes, which are then transferred to the edge engraving machine, the upper and lower flower embossing machines, and the silver dollar is roughly formed. It is then moved to the polishing machine in the next room to make it as shiny as new, and then dried with a machine. The next room is an automatic weighing machine that weighs the weight of the silver dollar, and an automatic machine that identifies the beauty of the silver dollar pattern. This is the last step of the work. At this point, the minting of the silver dollar is completed. The new silver dollars are placed in the silver dollar vault in the last room. The doors of each vault are purchased from the United States and are extremely strong. A large balance scale is placed opposite each to weigh the items at any time to avoid theft and leakage. The factory has 350 horsepower and 50 horsepower electric generators, and the equipment is extremely perfect. During the tour yesterday, the chief engineer, the American Heard, personally tested the purple copper bars, and the results were good.

Chinese and Foreign Businesses Closed Today 134

Today (18th), Chinese businesses are closed to commemorate the establishment of the capital in Nanjing, and Western businesses are also closed for Western holidays. Foreign banks are closed for four days from the 18th to the 21st. Chinese banks, except for China Communications and China Merchants, are closed as usual like foreign banks. The Central Bank and the Jianghai Customs are closed for one day today. On the exchange side, the gold industry is closed for four days and the securities are not.

Repeal of Restrictions on Yangtze River Navigation 141

▲ Night Navigation Returns to Normal

The Yangtze River waterway, due to the narrow waterway near Jiujiang during the previous low-water period, had issued an order prohibiting navigation at night. Now, due to the rising water level, this restriction has been completely lifted yesterday and the original state has been restored. Therefore, the departure times of the Yangtze River liner services have been changed again.

Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau Business Develops Rapidly 142

The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau of this city, as a state institution, serves the society, has solid guarantees, and complete facilities. Since its opening on March 15th, its business has been developing rapidly. The Director General of the Bureau, Liu Shufan, the Associate Director Shen Shuyu, and McLaren, along with all the staff, are working diligently. They are striving to popularize the interests of depositors. All savings regulations, such as current savings, fixed-term savings, and various methods such as lump-sum deposit and installment withdrawal, which will be added successively, are extremely simple, and the procedures are quick. There are also plans for a unified savings method, which is convenient for depositing and withdrawing money. This is an innovation in Shanghai. In the past, there were 25 post offices in the Shanghai area, but only 10 of them handled savings, and they were limited to deposit and withdrawal at the original branch, which was inconvenient for depositors. Now, all post offices in the city have opened savings branches, and they will be interconnected. For example, once an account is opened and money is deposited at the Shanghai General Bureau or a branch, money can be deposited and withdrawn at any post office in the Shanghai area at any time thereafter, allowing depositors to deposit money anywhere and withdraw money anywhere, avoiding the inconvenience of distance and the risk of carrying money on the road, and providing convenient home service. These advantages are not available in other savings institutions. The staff of the bureau have a lot of experience in savings business and are courteous, so people are happy to interact with them, and the business is developing rapidly.

The bureau's remittance business can be used for remittance to large and small cities at home and abroad, with low fees and easy withdrawal. In addition, referring to the successful methods of various countries, it is planning to handle transfer savings, which is especially convenient for merchants to transfer funds. As for the bureau's checks, all Chinese and foreign banks can collect and exchange them, which shows the completeness of the bureau's handling and the stability of its external credit.

▲ Seven Branch Bureaus to be Established Under its Jurisdiction in Nanjing and Other Places

The Ministry of Communications believes that China's navigation administration lacks a specialized bureau for management.
